            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the window becomes viewable and no earlier contents for it are remembered, the X server tiles the window with its background. If the window’s background is undefined, the existing screen contents are not altered, and the X server generates zero or more \textbf{Expose} events. If backing-store was maintained while the window was unmapped, no \textbf{Expose} events are generated. If backing-store will now be maintained, a full-window exposure is always generated. Otherwise, only visible regions may be reported. Similar tiling and exposure take place for any newly viewable inferiors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the window is an InputOutput window, \textbf{XMapWindow} generates Expose events on each InputOutput window that it causes to be displayed. If the client maps and paints the window and if the client begins processing events, the window is painted twice. To avoid this, first ask for Expose events and then map the window, so the client processes input events as usual. The event list will include Expose for each window that has appeared on the screen. The client’s normal response to an Expose event should be to repaint the window. This method usually leads to simpler programs and to proper interaction with window managers.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XMapWindow} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To map and raise a window, use \textbf{XMapRaised.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XMapRaised (display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The \textbf{XMapRaised} function essentially is similar to \textbf{XMapWindow} in that it maps the window and all of its subwindows that have had map requests. However, it also raises the specified window to the top of the stack. 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XMapRaised} can generate multiple \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To map all subwindows for a specified window, use \textbf{XMapSubwindows.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XMapSubwindows (display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The \textbf{XMapSubwindows} function maps all subwindows for a specified window in top-to-bottom stacking order. The X server generates Expose events on each newly displayed window. This may be much more efficient than mapping many windows one at a time because the server needs to perform much of the work only once, for all of the windows, rather than for each window.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XMapSubwindows} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
        \item \textbf{Unmapping Windows}: Xlib provides functions that you can use to unmap a window or all subwindows.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To unmap a window, use \textbf{XUnmapWindow.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XUnmapWindow(display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The \textbf{XUnmapWindow} function unmaps the specified window and causes the X server to generate an \textbf{UnmapNotify} event. If the specified window is already unmapped, \textbf{XUnmapWindow} has no effect. Normal exposure processing on formerly obscured windows is performed. Any child window will no longer be visible until another map call is made on the parent. In other words, the subwindows are still mapped but are not visible until the parent is mapped. Unmapping a window will generate Expose events on windows that were formerly obscured by it. 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XUnmapWindow} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To unmap all subwindows for a specified window, use \textbf{XUnmapSubwindows}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XUnmapSubwindows (display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            The \textbf{XUnmapSubwindows} function unmaps all subwindows for the specified window in bottom-to-top stacking order. It causes the X server to generate an \textbf{UnmapNotify} event on each subwindow and Expose events on formerly obscured windows. Using this function is much more efficient than unmapping multiple windows one at a time because the server needs to perform much of the work only once, for all of the windows, rather than for each window.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XUnmapSubwindows} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
        \item \textbf{Configuring Windows}: Xlib provides functions that you can use to move a window, resize a window, move and resize a window, or change a window’s border width. To change one of these parameters, set the appropriate member of the \textbf{XWindowChanges} structure and OR in the corresponding value mask in subsequent calls to \textbf{XConfigureWindow.} The symbols for the value mask bits and the \textbf{XWindowChanges} structure are
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                /* Configure window value mask bits */
                #define CWX                 (1<<0)
                #define CWY                 (1<<1)
                #define CWWidth             (1<<2)
                #define CWHeight            (1<<3)
                #define CWBorderWidth       (1<<4)
                #define CWSibling           (1<<5)
                #define CWStackMode         (1<<6)

                /* Values */

                typedef struct {
                    int x, y;
                    int width, height;
                    int border_width;
                    Window sibling;
                    int stack_mode;
                } XWindowChanges;
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The $x$ and $y$ members are used to set the window’s $x$ and $y$ coordinates, which are relative to the parent’s origin and indicate the position of the upper-left outer corner of the window. The width and height members are used to set the inside size of the window, not including the border, and must be nonzero, or a \textbf{BadValue} error results. Attempts to configure a root window have no effect.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The border\_width member is used to set the width of the border in pixels. Note that setting just the border width leaves the outer-left corner of the window in a fixed position but moves the absolute position of the window’s origin. If you attempt to set the border-width attribute of an \textbf{InputOnly} window nonzero, a \textbf{BadMatch} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{Note:} Inside the window, $(0,0)$ excludes the border. But when positioning the window relative to its parent, the position refers to the outer window, including the border.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The sibling member is used to set the sibling window for stacking operations. The stack\_mode member is used to set how the window is to be restacked and can be set to 
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textbf{Above}: Places the window above another window. Without \textbf{sibling} specified, it raises the window to the top. With sibling specified, it places that window above its specified sibling.
                \item \textbf{Below}: Places the window below another window. Without \textbf{sibling} specified, it raises the window to the bottom. With sibling specified, it places that window below its specified sibling.
                \item \textbf{TopIf}: 
                    Raises the window only if doing so is necessary. Informally: raise this window if it is currently being obscured.
                    \bigbreak \noindent 
                    Without sibling, X checks whether any sibling window is covering part of this window. If so, it raises the window to the top.
                    \bigbreak \noindent 
                    With sibling, X checks the relationship between this window and that sibling. If the sibling obscures this window, then this window is raised.
                \item \textbf{BottomIf}: Lowers the window only if doing so is necessary.
                    \bigbreak \noindent 
                    Without sibling, X checks whether this window is covering any sibling. If so, it lowers the window to the bottom.
                    \bigbreak \noindent 
                    With sibling, X checks whether this window obscures the given sibling. If so, this window is lowered.
                \item \textbf{Opposite}: This is conditional behavior based on whether the window is above or below another window.
                    \bigbreak \noindent 
                    Informally,
                    \begin{itemize}
                        \item if this window is being obscured, raise it;
                        \item if this window is obscuring another window, lower it
                    \end{itemize}
                    Without sibling, X compares the window against its siblings generally.
                    \bigbreak \noindent 
                    With sibling, X compares the window specifically against that sibling.
                    \bigbreak \noindent 
                    So Opposite can act like either \textbf{TopIf} or \textbf{BottomIf,} depending on the current overlap and stacking relationship.
            \end{itemize}
            If you do not specify a sibling, then stacking is relative to the whole sibling stack. For example, specifying \textbf{Above} will mean that a window gets raised to the top of its sibling stack.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If you specify sibling, then the operation is relative to that sibling window.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The sibling must actually be a sibling of the window being configured. That means both windows must have the same parent.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the override-redirect flag of the window is \textbf{False} and if some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent, the X server generates a ConfigureRequest event, and no further processing is performed. Otherwise, if some other client has selected \textbf{ResizeRedirectMask} on the window and the inside width or height of the window is being changed, a \textbf{ResizeRequest} event is generated, and the current inside width and height are used instead. Note that the override-redirect flag of the window has no effect on \textbf{ResizeRedirectMask} and that \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent has precedence over \textbf{ResizeRedirectMask} on the window.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            When the geometry of the window is changed as specified, the window is restacked among siblings, and a \textbf{ConfigureNotify} event is generated if the state of the window actually changes. \textbf{GravityNotify} events are generated after \textbf{ConfigureNotify} events. If the inside width or height of the window has actually changed, children of the window are affected as specified.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If a window’s size actually changes, the window’s subwindows move according to their window gravity. Depending on the window’s bit gravity, the contents of the window also may be moved.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If regions of the window were obscured but now are not, exposure processing is performed on these formerly obscured windows, including the window itself and its inferiors. As a result of increasing the width or height, exposure processing is also performed on any new regions of the window and any regions where window contents are lost
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The restack check (specifically, the computation for BottomIf, TopIf, and Opposite) is performed with respect to the window’s final size and position (as controlled by the other arguments of the request), not its initial position. If a sibling is specified without a stack\_mode, a BadMatch error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            Attempts to configure a root window have no effect.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To configure a window’s size, location, stacking, or border, use \textbf{XConfigureWindow}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XConfigureWindow(Display* display, Window w, unsigned int value_mask, XWindowChanges* values)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item value\_mask Specifies which values are to be set using information in the values structure. This mask is the bitwise inclusive OR of the valid configure window values bits.
                \item values Specifies the \textbf{XWindowChanges} structure.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XConfigureWindow} function uses the values specified in the \textbf{XWindowChanges} structure to reconfigure a window’s size, position, border, and stacking order. Values not specified are taken from the existing geometry of the window.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If a sibling is specified without a stack\_mode or if the window is not actually a sibling, a BadMatch error results. Note that the computations for \textbf{BottomIf,} \textbf{TopIf,} and Opposite are performed with respect to the window’s final geometry (as controlled by the other arguments passed to \textbf{XConfigureWindow),} not its initial geometry. Any backing store contents of the window, its inferiors, and other newly visible windows are either discarded or changed to reflect the current screen contents (depending on the implementation).
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XConfigureWindow} can generate \textbf{BadMatch,} \textbf{BadValue,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{Note:} A call to XConfigureWindow does cause the window to move in the stack (if specified in the mask), with respect to the specified configuration.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To move a window without changing its size, use \textbf{XMoveWindow.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XMoveWindow(display, w, x, y)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item $x$, $y$ Specify the $x$ and $y$ coordinates, which define the new location of the top-left pixel of the window’s border or the window itself if it has no border.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XMoveWindow} function moves the specified window to the specified $x$ and $y$ coordinates, but it does not change the window’s size, raise the window, or change the mapping state of the window. Moving a mapped window may or may not lose the window’s contents depending on if the window is obscured by non-children and if no backing store exists. If the contents of the window are lost, the X server generates Expose events. Moving a mapped window generates Expose events on any formerly obscured windows.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the override-redirect flag of the window is False and some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent, the X server generates a ConfigureRequest event, and no further processing is performed. Otherwise, the window is moved.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XMoveWindow} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To change a window’s size without changing the upper-left coordinate, use \textbf{XResizeWindow.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XResizeWindow(Display* display, Window w, unsigned int width, unsigned int height)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item width, height Specify the width and height, which are the interior dimensions of the window after the call completes.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XResizeWindow} function changes the inside dimensions of the specified window, not including its borders. This function does not change the window’s upper-left coordinate or the origin and does not restack the window. Changing the size of a mapped window may lose its contents and generate \textbf{Expose} events. If a mapped window is made smaller, changing its size generates \textbf{Expose} events on windows that the mapped window formerly obscured.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the override-redirect flag of the window is False and some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent, the X server generates a ConfigureRequest event, and no further processing is performed. If either width or height is zero, a \textbf{BadValue} error results.
            \textbf{XResizeWindow} can generate \textbf{BadValue} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To change the size and location of a window, use \textbf{XMoveResizeWindow.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XMoveResizeWindow(Display* display, Window w, int $x$, int y, unsigned int width, unsigned int height)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item $x$, $y$ Specify the $x$ and $y$ coordinates, which define the new position of the window relative to its parent.
                \item width, height Specify the width and height, which define the interior size of the window.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XMoveResizeWindow} function changes the size and location of the specified window without raising it. Moving and resizing a mapped window may generate an \textbf{Expose} event on the window. Depending on the new size and location parameters, moving and resizing a window may generate \textbf{Expose} events on windows that the window formerly obscured.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the override-redirect flag of the window is False and some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent, the X server generates a ConfigureRequest event, and no further processing is performed. Otherwise, the window size and location are changed.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XMoveResizeWindow} can generate \textbf{BadValue} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To change the border width of a given window, use \textbf{XSetWindowBorderWidth.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XSetWindowBorderWidth (Display* display, Window w, unsigned int width)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The \textbf{XSetWindowBorderWidth} function sets the specified window’s border width to the specified width. 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XSetWindowBorderWidth} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
        \item \textbf{Changing Window Stacking Order}: Xlib provides functions that you can use to raise, lower, circulate, or restack windows. 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To raise a window so that no sibling window obscures it, use XRaiseWindow.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XRaiseWindow(display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            The \textbf{XRaiseWindow} function raises the specified window to the top of the stack so that no sibling window obscures it. If the windows are regarded as overlapping sheets of paper stacked on a desk, then raising a window is analogous to moving the sheet to the top of the stack but leaving its $x$ and $y$ location on the desk constant. Raising a mapped window may generate \textbf{Expose} events for the window and any mapped subwindows that were formerly obscured.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the override-redirect attribute of the window is \textbf{False} and some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent, the X server generates a ConfigureRequest event, and no processing is performed. Otherwise, the window is raised.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XRaiseWindow} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To lower a window so that it does not obscure any sibling windows, use \textbf{XLowerWindow.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XLowerWindow(display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The \textbf{XLowerWindow} function lowers the specified window to the bottom of the stack so that it does not obscure any sibling windows. If the windows are regarded as overlapping sheets of paper stacked on a desk, then lowering a window is analogous to moving the sheet to the bottom of the stack but leaving its $x$ and $y$ location on the desk constant. Lowering a mapped window will generate \textbf{Expose} events on any windows it formerly obscured.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the override-redirect attribute of the window is \textbf{False} and some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent, the X server generates a \textbf{ConfigureRequest} event, and no processing is performed. Otherwise, the window is lowered to the bottom of the stack.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XLowerWindow} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To circulate a subwindow up or down, use \textbf{XCirculateSubwindows}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XCirculateSubwindows(Display* display, Window w, int direction)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item direction Specifies the direction (up or down) that you want to circulate the window. You can pass \textbf{RaiseLowest} or \textbf{LowerHighest.}
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XCirculateSubwindows} function circulates children of the specified window in the specified direction. If you specify \textbf{RaiseLowest,} \textbf{XCirculateSubwindows} raises the lowest mapped child (if any) that is occluded by another child to the top of the stack. If you specify \textbf{LowerHighest,} \textbf{XCirculateSubwindows} lowers the highest mapped child (if any) that occludes another child to the bottom of the stack. Exposure processing is then performed on formerly obscured windows. If some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the window, the X server generates a \textbf{CirculateRequest} event, and no further processing is performed. If a child is actually restacked, the X server generates a \textbf{CirculateNotify} event.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XCirculateSubwindows} can generate \textbf{BadValue} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To raise the lowest mapped child of a window that is partially or completely occluded by another child, use \textbf{XCirculateSubwindowsUp.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XCirculateSubwindowsUp (display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            The \textbf{XCirculateSubwindowsUp} function raises the lowest mapped child of the specified window that is partially or completely occluded by another child. Completely unobscured children are not affected. This is a convenience function equivalent to \textbf{XCirculateSubwindows} with \textbf{RaiseLowest} specified.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XCirculateSubwindowsUp can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To lower the highest mapped child of a window that partially or completely occludes another child, use \textbf{XCirculateSubwindowsDown}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XCirculateSubwindowsDown (display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            The \textbf{XCirculateSubwindowsDown} function lowers the highest mapped child of the specified window that partially or completely occludes another child. Completely unobscured children are not affected. This is a convenience function equivalent to \textbf{XCirculateSubwindows} with \textbf{LowerHighest} specified.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XCirculateSubwindowsDown} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To restack a set of windows from top to bottom, use \textbf{XRestackWindows.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XRestackWindows (Display* display, Window windows[], int nwindows);
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item windows Specifies an array containing the windows to be restacked.
                \item nwindows Specifies the number of windows to be restacked.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XRestackWindows} function restacks the windows in the order specified, from top to bottom. The stacking order of the first window in the windows array is unaffected, but the other windows in the array are stacked underneath the first window, in the order of the array. The stacking order of the other windows is not affected. For each window in the window array that is not a child of the specified window, a \textbf{BadMatch} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the override-redirect attribute of a window is False and some other client has selected \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask} on the parent, the X server generates \textbf{ConfigureRequest} events for each window whose override-redirect flag is not set, and no further processing is performed. Otherwise, the windows will be restacked in top-to-bottom order.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XRestackWindows} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
        \item \textbf{Changing window attributes}: Xlib provides functions that you can use to set window attributes. \textbf{XChangeWindowAttributes} is the more general function that allows you to set one or more window attributes provided by the XSetWindowAttributes structure. The other functions described in this section allow you to set one specific window attribute, such as a window’s background.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            Recall the \textbf{XSetWindowAttributes} structure
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                /* Window attribute value mask bits */
                #define CWBackPixmap        (1L<<0)
                #define CWBackPixel         (1L<<1)
                #define CWBorderPixmap      (1L<<2)
                #define CWBorderPixel       (1L<<3)
                #define CWBitGravity        (1L<<4)
                #define CWWinGravity        (1L<<5)
                #define CWBackingStore      (1L<<6)
                #define CWBackingPlanes     (1L<<7)
                #define CWBackingPixel      (1L<<8)
                #define CWOverrideRedirect  (1L<<9)
                #define CWSaveUnder         (1L<<10)
                #define CWEventMask         (1L<<11)
                #define CWDontPropagate     (1L<<12)
                #define CWColormap          (1L<<13)
                #define CWCursor            (1L<<14)

                typedef struct {
                    Pixmap background_pixmap;       /* background, None, or ParentRelative */
                    unsigned long background_pixel; /* background pixel */
                    Pixmap border_pixmap;           /* border of the window or CopyFromParent */
                    unsigned long border_pixel;     /* border pixel value */
                    int bit_gravity;                /* one of bit gravity values */
                    int win_gravity;                /* one of the window gravity values */
                    int backing_store;              /* NotUseful, WhenMapped, Always */
                    unsigned long backing_planes;   /* planes to be preserved if possible */
                    unsigned long backing_pixel;    /* value to use in restoring planes */
                    Bool save_under;                /* should bits under be saved? (popups) */
                    long event_mask;                /* set of events that should be saved */
                    long do_not_propagate_mask;     /* set of events that should not propagate */
                    Bool override_redirect;         /* boolean value for override_redirect */
                    Colormap colormap;              /* color map to be associated with window */
                    Cursor cursor;                  /* cursor to be displayed (or None) */
                } XSetWindowAttributes;
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To change one or more attributes for a given window, use \textbf{XChangeWindowAttributes}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XChangeWindowAttributes(Display* display, Window w, unsigned long valuemask, XSetWindowAttributes* attributes)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item valuemask Specifies which window attributes are defined in the attributes argument. This mask is the bitwise inclusive OR of the valid attribute mask bits. If valuemask is zero, the attributes are ignored and are not referenced. The values and restrictions are the same as for XCreateWindow.
                \item attributes Specifies the structure from which the values (as specified by the value mask) are to be taken. The value mask should have the appropriate bits set to indicate which attributes have been set in the structure
            \end{itemize}
            Depending on the valuemask, the \textbf{XChangeWindowAttributes} function uses the window attributes in the XSetWindowAttributes structure to change the specified window attributes. Changing the background does not cause the window contents to be changed. To repaint the window and its background, use \textbf{XClearWindow.} Setting the border or changing the background such that the border tile origin changes causes the border to be repainted. Changing the background of a root window to None or \textbf{ParentRelative} restores the default background pixmap. Changing the border of a root window to \textbf{CopyFromParent} restores the default border pixmap. Changing the win-gravity does not affect the current position of the window. Changing the backing-store of an obscured window to \textbf{WhenMapped} or Always, or changing the backing-planes, backing-pixel, or save-under of a mapped window may have no immediate effect. Changing the colormap of a window (that is, defining a new map, not changing the contents of the existing map) generates a \textbf{ColormapNotify} event. Changing the colormap of a visible window may have no immediate effect on the screen because the map may not be installed (see \textbf{XInstallColormap).} Changing the cursor of a root window to None restores the default cursor. Whenever possible, you are encouraged to share colormaps.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            Multiple clients can select input on the same window. Their event masks are maintained separately. When an event is generated, it is reported to all interested clients. However, only one client at a time can select for \textbf{SubstructureRedirectMask,} \textbf{ResizeRedirectMask,} and \textbf{ButtonPressMask.} If a client attempts to select any of these event masks and some other client has already selected one, a \textbf{BadAccess} error results. There is only one do-not-propagate-mask for a window, not one per client.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XChangeWindowAttributes} can generate \textbf{BadAccess,} \textbf{BadColor,} \textbf{BadCursor,} \textbf{BadMatch,} \textbf{BadPixmap,} \textbf{BadValue,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To set the background of a window to a given pixel, use \textbf{XSetWindowBackground}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XSetWindowBackground (Display* display, Window w, unsigned long background_pixel)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item background\_pixel Specifies the pixel that is to be used for the background.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XSetWindowBackground} function sets the background of the window to the specified pixel value. Changing the background does not cause the window contents to be changed. \textbf{XSetWindowBackground} uses a pixmap of undefined size filled with the pixel value you passed. If you try to change the background of an \textbf{InputOnly} window, a \textbf{BadMatch} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XSetWindowBackground} can generate \textbf{BadMatch} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To set the background of a window to a given pixmap, use \textbf{XSetWindowBackgroundPixmap.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XSetWindowBackgroundPixmap (Display* display, Window w, Pixmap background_pixmap)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The \textbf{XSetWindowBackgroundPixmap} function sets the background pixmap of the window to the specified pixmap. The background pixmap can immediately be freed if no further explicit references to it are to be made. If \textbf{ParentRelative} is specified, the background pixmap of the window’s parent is used, or on the root window, the default background is restored. If you try to change the background of an \textbf{InputOnly} window, a \textbf{BadMatch} error results. If the background is set to None, the window has no defined background.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XSetWindowBackgroundPixmap} can generate \textbf{BadMatch,} \textbf{BadPixmap,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{Note}: \textbf{XSetWindowBackground} and \textbf{XSetWindowBackgroundPixmap} do not change the current contents of the window.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To change and repaint a window’s border to a given pixel, use \textbf{XSetWindowBorder.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XSetWindowBorder (display, w, unsigned long border_pixel)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item border\_pixel Specifies the entry in the colormap.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XSetWindowBorder} function sets the border of the window to the pixel value you specify. If you attempt to perform this on an \textbf{InputOnly} window, a \textbf{BadMatch} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XSetWindowBorder} can generate \textbf{BadMatch} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To change and repaint the border tile of a given window, use XSetWindowBorderPixmap.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XSetWindowBorderPixmap (display, w, Pixmap border_pixmap)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item border\_pixmap Specifies the border pixmap or CopyFromParent.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XSetWindowBorderPixmap} function sets the border pixmap of the window to the pixmap you specify. The border pixmap can be freed immediately if no further explicit references to it are to be made. If you specify \textbf{CopyFromParent,} a copy of the parent window’s border pixmap is used. If you attempt to perform this on an \textbf{InputOnly} window, a \textbf{BadMatch} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XSetWindowBorderPixmap} can generate \textbf{BadMatch,} \textbf{BadPixmap,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To set the colormap of a given window, use \textbf{XSetWindowColormap.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XSetWindowColormap (display, w, Colormap colormap)
            \end{cppcode}
            The \textbf{XSetWindowColormap} function sets the specified colormap of the specified window. The colormap must have the same visual type as the window, or a \textbf{BadMatch} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XSetWindowColormap} can generate \textbf{BadColor,} \textbf{BadMatch,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To define which cursor will be used in a window, use \textbf{XDefineCursor}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XDefineCursor (display, w, Cursor cursor)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item cursor Specifies the cursor that is to be displayed or None.
            \end{itemize}
            If a cursor is set, it will be used when the pointer is in the window. If the cursor is None, it is equivalent to \textbf{XUndefineCursor.} \textbf{XDefineCursor} can generate BadCursor and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To undefine the cursor in a given window, use \textbf{XUndefineCursor.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XUndefineCursor (display, w)
            \end{cppcode}
            The \textbf{XUndefineCursor} function undoes the effect of a previous \textbf{XDefineCursor} for this window. When the pointer is in the window, the parent’s cursor will now be used. On the root window, the default cursor is restored.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XUndefineCursor} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.

    \end{itemize}

    \pagebreak 
    \unsect{4. Window information functions}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Intro}: After you connect the display to the X server and create a window, you can use the Xlib window information functions to:
            \begin{itemize}
                \item Obtain information about a window
                \item Translate screen coordinates
                \item Manipulate property lists
                \item Obtain and change window properties
                \item Manipulate selections
            \end{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Obtaining Window Information}: Xlib provides functions that you can use to obtain information about the window tree, the window’s current attributes, the window’s current geometry, or the current pointer coordinates. Because they are most frequently used by window managers, these functions all return a status to indicate whether the window still exists.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To obtain the parent, a list of children, and number of children for a given window, use \textbf{XQueryTree.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            Status XQueryTree (Display* display, Window w, Window* root_return, Window* parent_return, Window** children_return, unsigned int* nchildren_return)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item root\_return Returns the root window.
                \item parent\_return Returns the parent window.
                \item children\_return Returns the list of children.
                \item nchildren\_return Returns the number of children.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XQueryTree} function returns the root ID, the parent window ID, a pointer to the list of children windows (NULL when there are no children), and the number of children in the list for the specified window. The children are listed in current stacking order, from bottom-most (first) to top-most (last). \textbf{XQueryTree} returns zero if it fails and nonzero if it succeeds. To free a non-NULL children list when it is no longer needed, use \textbf{XFree.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XQueryTree} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To obtain the current attributes of a given window, use \textbf{XGetWindowAttributes.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XGetWindowAttributes (display, w, XWindowAttributes* window_attributes_return)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textbf{window\_attributes\_return}: Returns the specified window’s attributes in the XWindowAttributes structure.
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XGetWindowAttributes} function returns the current attributes for the specified window to an \textbf{XWindowAttributes} structure.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                typedef struct {
                    int x, y; /* location of window */
                    int width, height; /* width and height of window */
                    int border_width; /* border width of window */
                    int depth; /* depth of window */
                    Visual *visual; /* the associated visual structure */
                    Window root; /* root of screen containing window */
                    int class; /* InputOutput, InputOnly*/
                    int bit_gravity; /* one of the bit gravity values */
                    int win_gravity; /* one of the window gravity values */
                    int backing_store; /* NotUseful, WhenMapped, Always */
                    unsigned long backing_planes; /* planes to be preserved if possible */
                    unsigned long backing_pixel; /* value to be used when restoring planes */
                    Bool save_under; /* boolean, should bits under be saved? */
                    Colormap colormap; /* color map to be associated with window */
                    Bool map_installed; /* boolean, is color map currently installed*/
                    int map_state; /* IsUnmapped, IsUnviewable, IsViewable */
                    long all_event_masks; /* set of events all people have interest in*/
                    long your_event_mask; /* my event mask */
                    long do_not_propagate_mask; /* set of events that should not propagate */
                    Bool override_redirect; /* boolean value for override-redirect */
                    Screen *screen; /* back pointer to correct screen */
                } XWindowAttributes;
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The $x$ and $y$ members are set to the upper-left outer corner relative to the parent window’s origin. The width and height members are set to the inside size of the window, not including the border. The border\_width member is set to the window’s border width in pixels. The depth member is set to the depth of the window (that is, bits per pixel for the object). The visual member is a pointer to the screen’s associated \textbf{Visual} structure. The root member is set to the root window of the screen containing the window. The class member is set to the window’s class and can be either \textbf{InputOutput} or \textbf{InputOnly.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The bit\_gravity member is set to the window’s bit gravity and can be one of the following:
            \begin{itemize}
                \item ForgetGravity 
                \item EastGravity
                \item NorthWestGravity 
                \item SouthWestGravity
                \item NorthGravity 
                \item SouthGravity
                \item NorthEastGravity 
                \item SouthEastGravity
                \item WestGravity 
                \item StaticGravity
                \item CenterGravity
            \end{itemize}
            The win\_gravity member is set to the window’s window gravity and can be one of the following:
            \begin{itemize}
                \item UnmapGravity 
                \item EastGravity
                \item NorthWestGravity 
                \item SouthWestGravity
                \item NorthGravity 
                \item SouthGravity
                \item NorthEastGravity 
                \item SouthEastGravity
                \item WestGravity 
                \item StaticGravity
                \item CenterGravity
            \end{itemize}
            The backing\_store member is set to indicate how the X server should maintain the contents of a window and can be \textbf{WhenMapped,} Always, or \textbf{NotUseful.} The backing\_planes member is set to indicate (with bits set to 1) which bit planes of the window hold dynamic data that must be pre-served in backing\_stores and during save\_unders. The backing\_pixel member is set to indicate what values to use for planes not set in backing\_planes.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The save\_under member is set to True or False. The colormap member is set to the colormap for the specified window and can be a colormap ID or None. The map\_installed member is set to indicate whether the colormap is currently installed and can be True or False. The map\_state member is set to indicate the state of the window and can be \textbf{IsUnmapped,} \textbf{IsUnviewable,} or \textbf{IsViewable.} \textbf{IsUnviewable} is used if the window is mapped but some ancestor is unmapped.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The all\_event\_masks member is set to the bitwise inclusive OR of all event masks selected on the window by all clients. The your\_event\_mask member is set to the bitwise inclusive OR of all event masks selected by the querying client. The do\_not\_propagate\_mask member is set to the bitwise inclusive OR of the set of events that should not propagate.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The override\_redirect member is set to indicate whether this window overrides structure control facilities and can be True or False. Window manager clients should ignore the window if this member is True.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The screen member is set to a screen pointer that gives you a back pointer to the correct screen. This makes it easier to obtain the screen information without having to loop over the root window fields to see which field matches. \textbf{XGetWindowAttributes} can generate \textbf{BadDrawable} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To obtain the current geometry of a given drawable, use \textbf{XGetGeometry.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XGetGeometry(
                    Display* display, 
                    Drawable d,
                    Window* root_return,
                    int* x_return, int* y_return,
                    unsigned int* width_return, unsigned int* height_return,
                    unsigned int* border_width_return,
                    unsigned int* depth_return
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item d Specifies the drawable, which can be a window or a pixmap.
                \item root\_return Returns the root window.
                \item x\_return, y\_return Return the $x$ and $y$ coordinates that define the location of the drawable. For a window, these coordinates specify the upper-left outer corner relative to its parent’s origin. For pixmaps, these coordinates are always zero.
                \item width\_return, height\_return Return the drawable’s dimensions (width and height). For a window, these dimensions specify the inside size, not including the border.
                \item border\_width\_return Returns the border width in pixels. If the drawable is a pixmap, it returns zero.
                \item depth\_return Returns the depth of the drawable (bits per pixel for the object).
            \end{itemize}
            The \textbf{XGetGeometry} function returns the root window and the current geometry of the drawable. The geometry of the drawable includes the $x$ and $y$ coordinates, width and height, border width, and depth. These are described in the argument list. It is legal to pass to this function a window whose class is \textbf{InputOnly.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XGetGeometry} can generate a \textbf{BadDrawable} error.
        \item \textbf{Translating Screen Coordinates}: Applications sometimes need to perform a coordinate transformation from the coordinate space of one window to another window or need to determine which window the pointing device is in. \textbf{XTranslateCoordinates} and \textbf{XQueryPointer} fulfill these needs (and avoid any race conditions) by asking the X server to perform these operations.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To translate a coordinate in one window to the coordinate space of another window, use \textbf{XTranslateCoordinates.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Bool XTranslateCoordinates (
                    Display* display,
                    Window src_w, Window dest_w,
                    int src_x, int src_y,
                    int* dest_x_return, int* dest_y_return,
                    Window* child_return
            )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item src\_w Specifies the source window.
                \item dest\_w Specifies the destination window.
                \item src\_x, src\_y Specify the $x$ and $y$ coordinates within the source window.
                \item dest\_x\_return, dest\_y\_return Return the $x$ and $y$ coordinates within the destination window.
                \item child\_return Returns the child if the coordinates are contained in a mapped child of the destination window.
            \end{itemize}
            If \textbf{XTranslateCoordinates} returns \textbf{True,} it takes the src\_x and src\_y coordinates relative to the source window’s origin and returns these coordinates to dest\_x\_return and dest\_y\_return relative to the destination window’s origin. If \textbf{XTranslateCoordinates} returns \textbf{False,} src\_w and dest\_w are on different screens, and dest\_x\_return and dest\_y\_return are zero. If the coordinates are contained in a mapped child of dest\_w, that child is returned to child\_return. Otherwise, child\_return is set to \textbf{None.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \textbf{XTranslateCoordinates} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To obtain the screen coordinates of the pointer or to determine the pointer coordinates relative to a specified window, use \textbf{XQueryPointer.}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Bool XQueryPointer(
                    Display* display,
                    Window w,
                    Window* root_return, Window* child_return,
                    int* root_x_return, int* root_y_return,
                    int* win_x_return, int* win_y_return,
                    unsigned int* mask_return
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item $w$ Specifies the window.
                \item root\_return Returns the root window that the pointer is in.
                \item child\_return Returns the child window that the pointer is located in, if any.
                \item root\_x\_return, root\_y\_return Return the pointer coordinates relative to the root window’s origin.
                \item win\_x\_return, win\_y\_return Return the pointer coordinates relative to the specified window.
                \item mask\_return Returns the current state of the modifier keys and pointer buttons.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XQueryPointer} function returns the root window the pointer is logically on and the pointer coordinates relative to the root window’s origin. If \textbf{XQueryPointer} returns False, the pointer is not on the same screen as the specified window, and \textbf{XQueryPointer} returns None to child\_return and zero to win\_x\_return and win\_y\_return. If \textbf{XQueryPointer} returns True, the pointer coordinates returned to win\_x\_return and win\_y\_return are relative to the origin of the specified window. In this case, \textbf{XQueryPointer} returns the child that contains the pointer, if any, or else None to child\_return.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XQueryPointer} returns the current logical state of the keyboard buttons and the modifier keys in mask\_return. It sets mask\_return to the bitwise inclusive OR of one or more of the button or modifier key bitmasks to match the current state of the mouse buttons and the modifier keys. Note that the logical state of a device (as seen through Xlib) may lag the physical state if device event processing is frozen (see section 12.1).
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XQueryPointer} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
    \item \textbf{Properties}: In Xlib, a property is a piece of data attached to a window.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        Think of a window as having a small key-value database attached to it:
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{verbatim}
           Window
             |--- property: WM_NAME        -> "My Terminal"
             |--- property: WM_CLASS       -> "kitty"
             |--- property: WM_HINTS       -> window-manager hints
             |--- property: _NET_WM_STATE  -> fullscreen/maximized/etc. 
        \end{verbatim}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        Each property has three main parts:
        \begin{itemize}
            \item \textbf{name}:   what the property is called
            \item \textbf{type}:   what kind of data it stores
            \item \textbf{data}:   the actual bytes stored
        \end{itemize}
        For example, 
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            name: WM_NAME
            type: STRING
            data: "My Window"
        \end{cppcode}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        An \textbf{atom} is just a unique numeric ID for a string name.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            "WM_NAME"  -> atom 39
            "STRING"   -> atom 31
            "CARDINAL" -> atom 6
        \end{cppcode}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        So instead of repeatedly passing the string "WM\_NAME", Xlib passes the atom representing "WM\_NAME".
    \item \textbf{Properties and atoms}: A property is a collection of named, typed data. The window system has a set of predefined properties (for example, the name of a window, size hints, and so on), and users can define any other arbitrary information and associate it with windows. Each property has a name, which is an ISO Latin-1 string. For each named property, a unique identifier (\textbf{atom)} is associated with it. A property also has a type, for example, string or integer. These types are also indicated using atoms, so arbitrary new types can be defined. Data of only one type may be associated with a single property name. Clients can store and retrieve properties associated with windows. For efficiency reasons, an atom is used rather than a character string. \textbf{XInternAtom} can be used to obtain the atom for property names.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        A property is also stored in one of several possible formats. The X server can store the information as 8-bit quantities, 16-bit quantities, or 32-bit quantities. This permits the X server to present the data in the byte order that the client expects
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{Note:} If you define further properties of complex type, you must encode and decode them yourself. These functions must be carefully written if they are to be portable
        \bigbreak \noindent         
        The type of a property is defined by an atom, which allows for arbitrary extension in this type scheme.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        Certain property names are predefined in the server for commonly used functions. The atoms for these properties are defined in \textbf{<X11/Xatom.h>.} To avoid name clashes with user symbols, the \textbf{\#define} name for each atom has the \textbf{XA\_ prefix.} For an explanation of the functions that let you get and set much of the information stored in these predefined properties, see chapter 14.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        The core protocol imposes no semantics on these property names, but semantics are specified in other X Consortium standards, such as the Inter-Client Communication Conventions Manual and the X Logical Font Description Conventions.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        You can use properties to communicate other information between applications. The functions described in this section let you define new properties and get the unique atom IDs in your applications.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        Although any particular atom can have some client interpretation within each of the name spaces, atoms occur in five distinct name spaces within the protocol:
        \begin{itemize}
            \item Selections
            \item Property names
            \item Property types
            \item Font properties
            \item Type of a \textbf{ClientMessage} event (none are built into the X server)
        \end{itemize}
        The built-in selection property names are:
        \begin{verbatim}
            PRIMARY             SECONDARY
            CLIPBOARD
        \end{verbatim}
        The built-in property names are:
        \begin{verbatim}
            CUT_BUFFER0         RESOURCE_MANAGER
            CUT_BUFFER1         WM_CLASS
            CUT_BUFFER2         WM_CLIENT_MACHINE
            CUT_BUFFER3         WM_COLORMAP_WINDOWS
            CUT_BUFFER4         WM_COMMAND
            CUT_BUFFER5         WM_HINTS
            CUT_BUFFER6         WM_ICON_NAME
            CUT_BUFFER7         WM_ICON_SIZE
            RGB_BEST_MAP        WM_NAME
            RGB_BLUE_MAP        WM_NORMAL_HINTS
            RGB_DEFAULT_MAP     WM_PROTOCOLS
            RGB_GRAY_MAP        WM_STATE
            RGB_GREEN_MAP       WM_TRANSIENT_FOR
            RGB_RED_MAP         WM_ZOOM_HINTS
        \end{verbatim}
        The built-in property types are:
        \begin{verbatim}
            ARC                 POINT
            ATOM                RGB_COLOR_MAP
            BITMAP              RECTANGLE
            CARDINAL            STRING
            COLORMAP            VISUALID
            CURSOR              WINDOW
            DRAWABLE            WM_HINTS
            FONT                WM_SIZE_HINTS
            INTEGER
            PIXMAP 
        \end{verbatim}
        The built-in font property names are:
        \begin{verbatim}
            MIN_SPACE           STRIKEOUT_DESCENT
            NORM_SPACE          STRIKEOUT_ASCENT
            MAX_SPACE           ITALIC_ANGLE
            END_SPACE           X_HEIGHT
            SUPERSCRIPT_X       QUAD_WIDTH
            SUPERSCRIPT_Y       WEIGHT
            SUBSCRIPT_X         POINT_SIZE
            SUBSCRIPT_Y         RESOLUTION
            UNDERLINE_POSITION  COPYRIGHT
            UNDERLINE_THICKNESS NOTICE
            FONT_NAME           FAMILY_NAME
            FULL_NAME           CAP_HEIGHT 
        \end{verbatim}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            Atom XInternAtom(Display* display, char* atom_name, Bool only_if_exists)
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item atom\_name Specifies the name associated with the atom you want returned.
            \item only\_if\_exists Specifies a Boolean value that indicates whether the atom must be created.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XInternAtom} function returns the atom identifier associated with the specified atom\_name string. If only\_if\_exists is False, the atom is created if it does not exist. Therefore, \textbf{XInternAtom} can return None. If the atom name is not in the Host Portable Character Encoding, the result is implementation-dependent. Uppercase and lowercase matter; the strings ‘‘thing’’, ‘‘Thing’’, and ‘‘thinG’’ all designate different atoms. The atom will remain defined even after the client’s connection closes. It will become undefined only when the last connection to the X server closes.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XInternAtom} can generate BadAlloc and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To return atoms for an array of names, use \textbf{XInternAtoms.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            Status XInternAtoms(Display* display, char** names, int count, Bool only_if_exists, Atom* atoms_return)
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item names Specifies the array of atom names.
            \item count Specifies the number of atom names in the array.
            \item only\_if\_exists Specifies a Boolean value that indicates whether the atom must be created.
            \item atoms\_return Returns the atoms.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XInternAtoms} function returns the atom identifiers associated with the specified names. The atoms are stored in the atoms\_return array supplied by the caller. Calling this function is equivalent to calling \textbf{XInternAtom} for each of the names in turn with the specified value of only\_if\_exists, but this function minimizes the number of round-trip protocol exchanges between the client and the X server. This function returns a nonzero status if atoms are returned for all of the names; otherwise, it returns zero.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XInternAtoms} can generate BadAlloc and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To return a name for a given atom identifier, use \textbf{XGetAtomName.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
        char *XGetAtomName(Display display, Atom atom)
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item atom Specifies the atom for the property name you want returned.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XGetAtomName} function returns the name associated with the specified atom. If the data returned by the server is in the Latin Portable Character Encoding, then the returned string is in the Host Portable Character Encoding. Otherwise, the result is implementation-dependent. To free the resulting string, call \textbf{XFree.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XGetAtomName} can generate a \textbf{BadAtom} error.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To return the names for an array of atom identifiers, use \textbf{XGetAtomNames.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            Status XGetAtomNames(Display* display, Atom* atoms, int count, char** names_return)
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item atoms Specifies the array of atoms.
            \item count Specifies the number of atoms in the array.
            \item names\_return Returns the atom names.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XGetAtomNames} function returns the names associated with the specified atoms. The names are stored in the names\_return array supplied by the caller. Calling this function is equivalent to calling \textbf{XGetAtomName} for each of the atoms in turn, but this function minimizes the number of round-trip protocol exchanges between the client and the X server. This function returns a nonzero status if names are returned for all of the atoms; otherwise, it returns zero.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        XGetAtomNames can generate a BadAtom error.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{Note}: Note that 
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
        typedef unsigned long Atom;
        \end{cppcode}
    \item \textbf{Obtaining and Changing Window Properties}: You can attach a property list to every window. Each property has a name, a type, and a value. The value is an array of 8-bit, 16-bit, or 32-bit quantities, whose interpretation is left to the clients. The type char is used to represent 8-bit quantities, the type short is used to represent 16-bit quantities, and the type long is used to represent 32-bit quantities. 
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        Xlib provides functions that you can use to obtain, change, update, or interchange window properties. In addition, Xlib provides other utility functions for inter-client communication (chapter 14)
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To obtain the type, format, and value of a property of a given window, use \textbf{XGetWindowProperty}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            int XGetWindowProperty (
                Display* display,
                Window w,
                Atom property,
                long long_offset, long_length,
                Bool delete,
                Atom req_type,
                Atom* actual_type_return,
                int* actual_format_return,
                unsigned long* nitems_return,
                unsigned long* bytes_after_return,
                unsigned char** prop_return
            )
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item $w$ Specifies the window whose property you want to obtain.
            \item property Specifies the property name.
            \item long\_offset Specifies the offset in the specified property (in 32-bit quantities) where the data is to be retrieved.
            \item long\_length Specifies the length in 32-bit multiples of the data to be retrieved.
            \item delete Specifies a Boolean value that determines whether the property is deleted.
            \item req\_type Specifies the atom identifier associated with the property type or \textbf{AnyPropertyType}.
            \item actual\_type\_return Returns the atom identifier that defines the actual type of the property.
            \item actual\_format\_return Returns the actual format of the property.
            \item nitems\_return Returns the actual number of 8-bit, 16-bit, or 32-bit items stored in the prop\_return data.
            \item bytes\_after\_return Returns the number of bytes remaining to be read in the property if a partial read was performed.
            \item prop\_return Returns the data in the specified format.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} function returns the actual type of the property; the actual format of the property; the number of 8-bit, 16-bit, or 32-bit items transferred; the number of bytes remaining to be read in the property; and a pointer to the data actually returned. \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} sets the return arguments as follows:
        \begin{itemize}
            \item If the specified property does not exist for the specified window, \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} returns \textbf{None} to actual\_type\_return and the value zero to actual\_format\_return and bytes\_after\_return. The nitems\_return argument is empty. In this case, the delete argument is ignored.
            \item If the specified property exists but its type does not match the specified type, \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} returns the actual property type to actual\_type\_return, the actual property format (never zero) to actual\_format\_return, and the property length in bytes (even if the actual\_format\_return is 16 or 32) to bytes\_after\_return. It also ignores the delete argument. The nitems\_return argument is empty.
            \item If the specified property exists and either you assign \textbf{AnyPropertyType} to the req\_type argument or the specified type matches the actual property type, \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} returns the actual property type to actual\_type\_return and the actual property format (never zero) to actual\_format\_return. It also returns a value to bytes\_after\_return and nitems\_return, by defining the following values:
                \begin{align*}
                    N &= \text{actual length of the stored property in bytes} \\
                    I &= 4 \cdot \text{long\_offset} \\
                    T &= N - I \\
                    L &= \min(T, 4\cdot \text{long\_length}) \\
                    A &= N - (I+L)
                .\end{align*}
                The returned value starts at byte index $I$ in the property (indexing from zero), and its length in bytes is $L$. If the value for long\_offset causes $L$ to be negative, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. The value of bytes\_after\_return is $A$, giving the number of trailing unread bytes in the stored property.
        \end{itemize}
        \textbf{Note}: \texttt{Bool delete} specifies whether $X$ should delete the property after reading it. It only actually deletes the property if the read succeeds and there are no unread bytes left, meaning \texttt{bytes\_after\_return = 0}.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        If you pass a specific type and the property has a different actual type, Xlib tells you the actual type but does not return the property data in the normal way.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        For 
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
        int* actual_format_return
        \end{cppcode}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        Xlib writes the property's data form here. The format is usually one of
        \begin{itemize}
            \item 8 $\implies $ data is 8-bit quantities
            \item 16 $\implies$ data is 16-bit quantities
            \item 32 $\implies$ data is 32-bit quantities
        \end{itemize}
        This tells us how to interpret \texttt{prop\_return}.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        If the returned format is 8, the returned data is represented as a \textbf{char} array. If the returned format is 16, the returned data is represented as a \textbf{short} array and should be cast to that type to obtain the elements. If the returned format is 32, the returned data is represented as a \textbf{long} array and should be cast to that type to obtain the elements.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} always allocates one extra byte in prop\_return (even if the property is zero length) and sets it to zero so that simple properties consisting of characters do not have to be copied into yet another string before use.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        If delete is True and bytes\_after\_return is zero, \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} deletes the property
        from the window and generates a \textbf{PropertyNotify} event on the window.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        The function returns \textbf{Success} if it executes successfully. To free the resulting data, use \textbf{XFree.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XGetWindowProperty} can generate \textbf{BadAtom,} \textbf{BadValue,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To obtain a given window’s property list, use \textbf{XListProperties.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            Atom* XListProperties(Display* display, Window w, int* num_prop_return)
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item $w$ Specifies the window whose property list you want to obtain.
            \item num\_prop\_return Returns the length of the properties array.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XListProperties} function returns a pointer to an array of atom properties that are defined for the specified window or returns NULL if no properties were found. To free the memory allocated by this function, use \textbf{XFree.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XListProperties} can generate a \textbf{BadWindow} error.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To change a property of a given window, use \textbf{XChangeProperty}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            XChangeProperty (
                Display* display,
                Window w,
                Atom property, type,
                int format,
                int mode,
                unsigned char* data,
                int nelements
            )
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item $w$ Specifies the window whose property you want to change.
            \item property Specifies the property name.
            \item type Specifies the type of the property. The X server does not interpret the type but simply passes it back to an application that later calls \textbf{XGetWindowProperty.}
            \item format Specifies whether the data should be viewed as a list of 8-bit, 16-bit, or 32-bit quantities. Possible values are 8, 16, and 32. This information allows the X server to correctly perform byte-swap operations as necessary. If the format is 16-bit or 32-bit, you must explicitly cast your data pointer to an (unsigned char *) in the call to \textbf{XChangeProperty.}
            \item mode Specifies the mode of the operation. You can pass \textbf{PropModeReplace,} \textbf{PropModePrepend,} or \textbf{PropModeAppend.}
            \item data Specifies the property data.
            \item nelements Specifies the number of elements of the specified data format.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XChangeProperty} function alters the property for the specified window and causes the X server to generate a \textbf{PropertyNotify} event on that window. \textbf{XChangeProperty} performs the following:
        \begin{itemize}
            \item If mode is \textbf{PropModeReplace,} \textbf{XChangeProperty} discards the previous property value and stores the new data.
            \item If mode is \textbf{PropModePrepend} or \textbf{PropModeAppend,} \textbf{XChangeProperty} inserts the specified data before the beginning of the existing data or onto the end of the existing data, respectively. The type and format must match the existing property value, or a \textbf{BadMatch} error results. If the property is undefined, it is treated as defined with the correct type and format with zero-length data.
        \end{itemize}
        If the specified format is 8, the property data must be a \textbf{char} array. If the specified format is 16, the property data must be a \textbf{short} array. If the specified format is 32, the property data must be a \textbf{long} array.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        The lifetime of a property is not tied to the storing client. Properties remain until explicitly deleted, until the window is destroyed, or until the server resets. The maximum size of a property is server dependent and can vary dynamically depending on the amount of memory the server has available. (If there is insufficient space, a BadAlloc error results.)
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XChangeProperty} can generate BadAlloc, \textbf{BadAtom,} \textbf{BadMatch,} \textbf{BadValue,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To rotate a window’s property list, use \textbf{XRotateWindowProperties.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            XRotateWindowProperties (display, w, properties, num_prop, npositions)
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item $w$ Specifies the window.
            \item properties Specifies the array of properties that are to be rotated.
            \item num\_prop Specifies the length of the properties array.
            \item npositions Specifies the rotation amount.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XRotateWindowProperties} function allows you to rotate properties on a window and causes the X server to generate \textbf{PropertyNotify} events. If the property names in the properties array are viewed as being numbered starting from zero and if there are num\_prop property names in the list, then the value associated with property name $I$ becomes the value associated with property name $(I + \text{npositions}) \text{mod} N$ for all $I$ from zero to $N - 1$. The effect is to rotate the states by npositions places around the virtual ring of property names (right for positive npositions, left for negative npositions). If npositions mod $N$ is nonzero, the X server generates a \textbf{PropertyNotify} event for each property in the order that they are listed in the array. If an atom occurs more than once in the list or no property with that name is defined for the window, a \textbf{BadMatch} error results. If a \textbf{BadAtom} or \textbf{BadMatch} error results, no properties are changed.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XRotateWindowProperties} can generate \textbf{BadAtom,} \textbf{BadMatch,} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XRotateWindowProperties} is a niche convenience function for swapping property values among several property names on the same window.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        It does not rotate the bytes inside one property. It rotates which property name owns which value.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        Suppose a window has three properties:
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            P0 = "red"
            P1 = "green"
            P2 = "blue"
        \end{cppcode}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        and you call
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            Atom props[] = { P0, P1, P2 };
            XRotateWindowProperties(display, w, props, 3, 1);
        \end{cppcode}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        With $\text{npositions} = 1$, the value associated with property $I$ moves to property $(I + 1) \text{mod} 3$.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{itemize}
            \item P0's old value moves to P1
            \item P1's old value moves to P2
            \item P2's old value moves to P0
        \end{itemize}
        \begin{cppcode}
            P0 = "blue"
            P1 = "red"
            P2 = "green"
        \end{cppcode}

        \bigbreak \noindent 
        To delete a property on a given window, use \textbf{XDeleteProperty.}
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \begin{cppcode}
            XDeleteProperty (display, w, property)
        \end{cppcode}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \item $w$ Specifies the window whose property you want to delete.
            \item property Specifies the property name.
        \end{itemize}
        The \textbf{XDeleteProperty} function deletes the specified property only if the property was defined on the specified window and causes the X server to generate a \textbf{PropertyNotify} event on the window unless the property does not exist.
        \bigbreak \noindent 
        \textbf{XDeleteProperty} can generate \textbf{BadAtom} and \textbf{BadWindow} errors.
    \item \textbf{Selections}: Selections are one method used by applications to exchange data. By using the property mechanism, applications can exchange data of arbitrary types and can negotiate the type of the data. A selection can be thought of as an indirect property with a dynamic type. That is, rather than having the property stored in the X server, the property is maintained by some client (the owner).
