            Read-only colormap cells are shared among clients. The server counts each allocation and freeing of the cell by clients. When the last client frees a shared cell, the cell is finally deallocated. If a single client allocates the same read-only cell multiple times, the server counts each such allocation, not just the first one.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To allocate a read-only color cell with an RGB value, use \textbf{XAllocColor}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XAllocColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XColor *screen_in_out
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{screen\_in\_out}: Specifies and returns the values actually used in the colormap.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XAllocColor} function allocates a read-only colormap entry corresponding to the closest RGB value supported by the hardware. \textbf{XAllocColor} returns the pixel value of the closest to the specified RGB elements supported by the hardware and returns the RGB value actually used. The corresponding colormap cell is read-only. In addition, \textbf{XAllocColor} returns nonzero if it succeeded or zero if it failed. Multiple clients that request the same effective RGB value can be assigned the same read-only entry, thus allowing entries to be shared. When the last client deallocates a shared cell, it is deallocated. \textbf{XAllocColor} does not use or affect the flags in the \textbf{XColor} structure.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XAllocColor} can generate a \textbf{BadColor} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To allocate a read-only color cell with a color in arbitrary format, use \textbf{XcmsAllocColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XcmsAllocColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XcmsColor *color_in_out,
                    XcmsColorFormat result_format
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color\_in\_out}: Specifies the color to allocate and returns the pixel and color that is actually used in the colormap.
                \item \textit{result\_format}: Specifies the color format for the returned color specification.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XcmsAllocColor} function is similar to \textbf{XAllocColor} except the color can be specified in any format. The \textbf{XcmsAllocColor} function ultimately calls \textbf{XAllocColor} to allocate a read-only color cell, or colormap entry, with the specified color. \textbf{XcmsAllocColor} first converts the color specified in \textit{color\_in\_out} to an RGB value and then passes it to \textbf{XAllocColor}. \textbf{XcmsAllocColor} returns the pixel value of the color cell and the color specification actually allocated. This returned color specification is the result of converting the RGB value returned by \textbf{XAllocColor} into the format specified with the \textit{result\_format} argument. If there is no interest in a returned color specification, unnecessary computation can be bypassed if \textit{result\_format} is set to \textbf{XcmsRGBFormat}. The corresponding colormap cell is read-only. If this routine returns \textbf{XcmsFailure}, the \textit{color\_in\_out} color specification is left unchanged.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XcmsAllocColor} can generate a \textbf{BadColor} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To allocate a read-only color cell using a color name and return the closest color supported by the hardware in RGB format, use \textbf{XAllocNamedColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XAllocNamedColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    char *color_name,
                    XColor *screen_def_return,
                    XColor *exact_def_return
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color\_name}: Specifies the color name string, for example, \texttt{red}, whose color definition structure you want returned.
                \item \textit{screen\_def\_return}: Returns the closest RGB values provided by the hardware.
                \item \textit{exact\_def\_return}: Returns the exact RGB values.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XAllocNamedColor} function looks up the named color with respect to the screen that is associated with the specified colormap. It returns both the exact database definition and the closest color supported by the screen. The allocated color cell is read-only. The pixel value is returned in \textit{screen\_def\_return}. If the color name is not in the Host Portable Character Encoding, the result is implementation-dependent. Use of uppercase or lowercase does not matter. If \textit{screen\_def\_return} and \textit{exact\_def\_return} point to the same structure, the pixel field will be set correctly, but the color values are undefined. \textbf{XAllocNamedColor} returns nonzero if a cell is allocated; otherwise, it returns zero.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XAllocNamedColor} can generate a \textbf{BadColor} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To allocate a read-only color cell using a color name and return the closest color supported by the hardware in an arbitrary format, use \textbf{XcmsAllocNamedColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XcmsAllocNamedColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    char *color_string,
                    XcmsColor *color_screen_return,
                    XcmsColor *color_exact_return,
                    XcmsColorFormat result_format
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color\_string}: Specifies the color string whose color definition structure is to be returned.
                \item \textit{color\_screen\_return}: Returns the pixel value of the color cell and color specification that actually is stored for that cell.
                \item \textit{color\_exact\_return}: Returns the color specification parsed from the color string or parsed from the corresponding string found in a color-name database.
                \item \textit{result\_format}: Specifies the color format for the returned color specifications, namely the \textit{color\_screen\_return} and \textit{color\_exact\_return} arguments. If the format is \textbf{XcmsUndefinedFormat} and the color string contains a numerical color specification, the specification is returned in the format used in that numerical color specification. If the format is \textbf{XcmsUndefinedFormat} and the color string contains a color name, the specification is returned in the format used to store the color in the database.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XcmsAllocNamedColor} function is similar to \textbf{XAllocNamedColor} except that the color returned can be in any format specified. This function ultimately calls \textbf{XAllocColor} to allocate a read-only color cell with the color specified by a color string. The color string is parsed into an \textbf{XcmsColor} structure, converted to an RGB value, and finally passed to \textbf{XAllocColor}. If the color name is not in the Host Portable Character Encoding, the result is implementation-dependent. Use of uppercase or lowercase does not matter.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            This function returns both the color specification as a result of parsing, called the exact specification, and the actual color specification stored, called the screen specification. This screen specification is the result of converting the RGB value returned by \textbf{XAllocColor} into the format specified in \textit{result\_format}. If there is no interest in a returned color specification, unnecessary computation can be bypassed if \textit{result\_format} is set to \textbf{XcmsRGBFormat}. If \textit{color\_screen\_return} and \textit{color\_exact\_return} point to the same structure, the pixel field will be set correctly, but the color values are undefined.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XcmsAllocNamedColor} can generate a \textbf{BadColor} error.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To allocate read/write color cell and color plane combinations for a \textbf{PseudoColor} model, use \textbf{XAllocColorCells}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XAllocColorCells(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    Bool contig,
                    unsigned long plane_masks_return[],
                    unsigned int nplanes,
                    unsigned long pixels_return[],
                    unsigned int npixels
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{contig}: Specifies a Boolean value that indicates whether the planes must be contiguous.
                \item \textit{plane\_masks\_return}: Returns an array of plane masks.
                \item \textit{nplanes}: Specifies the number of plane masks that are to be returned in the plane masks array.
                \item \textit{pixels\_return}: Returns an array of pixel values.
                \item \textit{npixels}: Specifies the number of pixel values that are to be returned in the \textit{pixels\_return} array.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XAllocColorCells} function allocates read/write color cells. The number of colors must be positive and the number of planes nonnegative, or a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If \textit{npixels} and \textit{nplanes} are requested, then \textit{npixels} pixels and \textit{nplanes} plane masks are returned. No mask will have any bits set to 1 in common with any other mask or with any of the pixels. By ORing together each pixel with zero or more masks, $\textit{npixels} \times 2^{\textit{nplanes}}$ distinct pixels can be produced. All of these are allocated writable by the request.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            For \textbf{GrayScale} or \textbf{PseudoColor}, each mask has exactly one bit set to 1. For \textbf{DirectColor}, each has exactly three bits set to 1. If \textit{contig} is \textbf{True} and if all masks are ORed together, a single contiguous set of bits set to 1 will be formed for \textbf{GrayScale} or \textbf{PseudoColor}, and three contiguous sets of bits set to 1, one within each pixel subfield, for \textbf{DirectColor}. The RGB values of the allocated entries are undefined. \textbf{XAllocColorCells} returns nonzero if it succeeded or zero if it failed.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XAllocColorCells} can generate \textbf{BadColor} and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To allocate read/write color resources for a \textbf{DirectColor} model, use \textbf{XAllocColorPlanes}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The server guarantees that the returned masks do not overlap with each other or with the base pixels. That guarantee matters because otherwise ORing the masks together could accidentally collide with other allocated pixel values.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XAllocColorPlanes(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    Bool contig,
                    unsigned long pixels_return[],
                    int ncolors,
                    int nreds,
                    int ngreens,
                    int nblues,
                    unsigned long *rmask_return,
                    unsigned long *gmask_return,
                    unsigned long *bmask_return
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{contig}: Specifies a Boolean value that indicates whether the planes must be contiguous.
                \item \textit{pixels\_return}: Returns an array of pixel values. \textbf{XAllocColorPlanes} returns the pixel values in this array.
                \item \textit{ncolors}: Specifies the number of pixel values that are to be returned in the \textit{pixels\_return} array.
                \item \textit{nreds}: Specifies the number of red planes. The value you pass must be nonnegative.
                \item \textit{ngreens}: Specifies the number of green planes. The value you pass must be nonnegative.
                \item \textit{nblues}: Specifies the number of blue planes. The value you pass must be nonnegative.
                \item \textit{rmask\_return}: Returns the bit mask for the red planes.
                \item \textit{gmask\_return}: Returns the bit mask for the green planes.
                \item \textit{bmask\_return}: Returns the bit mask for the blue planes.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The specified \textit{ncolors} must be positive, and \textit{nreds}, \textit{ngreens}, and \textit{nblues} must be nonnegative, or a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If \textit{ncolors} colors, \textit{nreds} reds, \textit{ngreens} greens, and \textit{nblues} blues are requested, \textit{ncolors} pixels are returned, and the masks have \textit{nreds}, \textit{ngreens}, and \textit{nblues} bits set to 1, respectively. If \textit{contig} is \textbf{True}, each mask will have a contiguous set of bits set to 1. No mask will have any bits set to 1 in common with any other mask or with any of the pixels.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            For \textbf{DirectColor}, each mask will lie within the corresponding pixel subfield. By ORing together subsets of masks with each pixel value, $\textit{ncolors} \times 2^{(\textit{nreds} + \textit{ngreens} + \textit{nblues})}$ distinct pixel values can be produced. All of these are allocated by the request.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            However, in the colormap, there are only $\textit{ncolors} \times 2^{\textit{nreds}}$ independent red entries, $\textit{ncolors} \times 2^{\textit{ngreens}}$ independent green entries, and $\textit{ncolors} \times 2^{\textit{nblues}}$ independent blue entries. This is true even for \textbf{PseudoColor}. When the colormap entry of a pixel value is changed using \textbf{XStoreColors}, \textbf{XStoreColor}, or \textbf{XStoreNamedColor}, the pixel is decomposed according to the masks, and the corresponding independent entries are updated. \textbf{XAllocColorPlanes} returns nonzero if it succeeded or zero if it failed.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XAllocColorPlanes} can generate \textbf{BadColor} and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{Note:} The contig argument controls the shape of those masks. If contig is False, the server may return masks using any non-overlapping bit positions. 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                mask0 = 0b00000001
                mask1 = 0b00001000
                mask2 = 0b00100000
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            These masks are valid because they do not overlap, but the set of mask bits is not contiguous.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If contig is True, the server must return masks whose set bits form a contiguous range.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                mask0 = 0b00000100
                mask1 = 0b00001000
                mask2 = 0b00010000
            \end{cppcode}
            Together, these occupy adjacent bit positions:
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            0b00011100
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            For DirectColor, each mask affects the red, green, and blue subfields separately. So contig = True means there is a contiguous set of bits within each color subfield.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To free colormap cells, use \textbf{XFreeColors}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                int XFreeColors(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    unsigned long pixels[],
                    int npixels,
                    unsigned long planes
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{pixels}: Specifies an array of pixel values that map to the cells in the specified colormap.
                \item \textit{npixels}: Specifies the number of pixels.
                \item \textit{planes}: Specifies the planes you want to free.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XFreeColors} function frees the cells represented by pixels whose values are in the \textit{pixels} array. The \textit{planes} argument should not have any bits set to 1 in common with any of the pixels. The set of all pixels is produced by ORing together subsets of the \textit{planes} argument with the pixels.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            The request frees all of these pixels that were allocated by the client using \textbf{XAllocColor}, \textbf{XAllocNamedColor}, \textbf{XAllocColorCells}, and \textbf{XAllocColorPlanes}. Note that freeing an individual pixel obtained from \textbf{XAllocColorPlanes} may not actually allow it to be reused until all of its related pixels are also freed. Similarly, a read-only entry is not actually freed until it has been freed by all clients, and if a client allocates the same read-only entry multiple times, it must free the entry that many times before the entry is actually freed.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            All specified pixels that are allocated by the client in the colormap are freed, even if one or more pixels produce an error. If a specified pixel is not a valid index into the colormap, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If a specified pixel is not allocated by the client, that is, if it is unallocated or is only allocated by another client, or if the colormap was created with all entries writable by passing \textbf{AllocAll} to \textbf{XCreateColormap}, a \textbf{BadAccess} error results. If more than one pixel is in error, the one that gets reported is arbitrary.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XFreeColors} can generate \textbf{BadAccess}, \textbf{BadColor}, and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
        \item \textbf{Modifying and Querying Colormap Cells}: To store an RGB value in a single colormap cell, use \textbf{XStoreColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \begin{cppcode}
                int XStoreColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XColor *color
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color}: Specifies the pixel and RGB values.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XStoreColor} function changes the colormap entry of the pixel value specified in the \textit{pixel} member of the \textbf{XColor} structure. This pixel value must be a read/write cell and a valid index into the colormap. If a specified pixel is not a valid index into the colormap, a \textbf{BadValue} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XStoreColor} also changes the red, green, and/or blue color components. You specify which color components are to be changed by setting \textbf{DoRed}, \textbf{DoGreen}, and/or \textbf{DoBlue} in the \textit{flags} member of the \textbf{XColor} structure. If the colormap is an installed map for its screen, the changes are visible immediately.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XStoreColor} can generate \textbf{BadAccess}, \textbf{BadColor}, and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To store multiple RGB values in multiple colormap cells, use \textbf{XStoreColors}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \begin{cppcode}
                int XStoreColors(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XColor color[],
                    int ncolors
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color}: Specifies an array of color definition structures to be stored.
                \item \textit{ncolors}: Specifies the number of \textbf{XColor} structures in the color definition array.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XStoreColors} function changes the colormap entries of the pixel values specified in the \textit{pixel} members of the \textbf{XColor} structures. You specify which color components are to be changed by setting \textbf{DoRed}, \textbf{DoGreen}, and/or \textbf{DoBlue} in the \textit{flags} member of the \textbf{XColor} structures. If the colormap is an installed map for its screen, the changes are visible immediately.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XStoreColors} changes the specified pixels if they are allocated writable in the colormap by any client, even if one or more pixels generates an error. If a specified pixel is not a valid index into the colormap, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If a specified pixel either is unallocated or is allocated read-only, a \textbf{BadAccess} error results. If more than one pixel is in error, the one that gets reported is arbitrary.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XStoreColors} can generate \textbf{BadAccess}, \textbf{BadColor}, and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To store a color of arbitrary format in a single colormap cell, use \textbf{XcmsStoreColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XcmsStoreColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XcmsColor *color
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color}: Specifies the color cell and the color to store. Values specified in this \textbf{XcmsColor} structure remain unchanged on return.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XcmsStoreColor} function converts the color specified in the \textbf{XcmsColor} structure into RGB values. It then uses this RGB specification in an \textbf{XColor} structure, whose three flags, \textbf{DoRed}, \textbf{DoGreen}, and \textbf{DoBlue}, are set, in a call to \textbf{XStoreColor} to change the color cell specified by the \textit{pixel} member of the \textbf{XcmsColor} structure.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            This pixel value must be a valid index for the specified colormap, and the color cell specified by the pixel value must be a read/write cell. If the pixel value is not a valid index, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If the color cell is unallocated or is allocated read-only, a \textbf{BadAccess} error results. If the colormap is an installed map for its screen, the changes are visible immediately.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            Note that \textbf{XStoreColor} has no return value; therefore, an \textbf{XcmsSuccess} return value from this function indicates that the conversion to RGB succeeded and the call to \textbf{XStoreColor} was made. To obtain the actual color stored, use \textbf{XcmsQueryColor}. Because of the screen's hardware limitations or gamut compression, the color stored in the colormap may not be identical to the color specified.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XcmsStoreColor} can generate \textbf{BadAccess}, \textbf{BadColor}, and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To store multiple colors of arbitrary format in multiple colormap cells, use \textbf{XcmsStoreColors}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XcmsStoreColors(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XcmsColor colors[],
                    int ncolors,
                    Bool compression_flags_return[]
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{colors}: Specifies the color specification array of \textbf{XcmsColor} structures, each specifying a color cell and the color to store in that cell. Values specified in the array remain unchanged upon return.
                \item \textit{ncolors}: Specifies the number of \textbf{XcmsColor} structures in the color-specification array.
                \item \textit{compression\_flags\_return}: Returns an array of Boolean values indicating compression status. If a non-\textbf{NULL} pointer is supplied, each element of the array is set to \textbf{True} if the corresponding color was compressed and \textbf{False} otherwise. Pass \textbf{NULL} if the compression status is not useful.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XcmsStoreColors} function converts the colors specified in the array of \textbf{XcmsColor} structures into RGB values and then uses these RGB specifications in \textbf{XColor} structures, whose three flags, \textbf{DoRed}, \textbf{DoGreen}, and \textbf{DoBlue}, are set, in a call to \textbf{XStoreColors} to change the color cells specified by the \textit{pixel} member of the corresponding \textbf{XcmsColor} structure.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            Each pixel value must be a valid index for the specified colormap, and the color cell specified by each pixel value must be a read/write cell. If a pixel value is not a valid index, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If a color cell is unallocated or is allocated read-only, a \textbf{BadAccess} error results. If more than one pixel is in error, the one that gets reported is arbitrary. If the colormap is an installed map for its screen, the changes are visible immediately.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            Note that \textbf{XStoreColors} has no return value; therefore, an \textbf{XcmsSuccess} return value from this function indicates that conversions to RGB succeeded and the call to \textbf{XStoreColors} was made. To obtain the actual colors stored, use \textbf{XcmsQueryColors}. Because of the screen's hardware limitations or gamut compression, the colors stored in the colormap may not be identical to the colors specified.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XcmsStoreColors} can generate \textbf{BadAccess}, \textbf{BadColor}, and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To store a color specified by name in a single colormap cell, use \textbf{XStoreNamedColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                int XStoreNamedColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    char *color,
                    unsigned long pixel,
                    int flags
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color}: Specifies the color name string, for example, \texttt{red}.
                \item \textit{pixel}: Specifies the entry in the colormap.
                \item \textit{flags}: Specifies which red, green, and blue components are set.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XStoreNamedColor} function looks up the named color with respect to the screen associated with the colormap and stores the result in the specified colormap. The \textit{pixel} argument determines the entry in the colormap. The \textit{flags} argument determines which of the red, green, and blue components are set. You can set this member to the bitwise inclusive OR of the bits \textbf{DoRed}, \textbf{DoGreen}, and \textbf{DoBlue}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            If the color name is not in the Host Portable Character Encoding, the result is implementation-dependent. Use of uppercase or lowercase does not matter. If the specified pixel is not a valid index into the colormap, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If the specified pixel either is unallocated or is allocated read-only, a \textbf{BadAccess} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XStoreNamedColor} can generate \textbf{BadAccess}, \textbf{BadColor}, \textbf{BadName}, and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            The \textbf{XQueryColor} and \textbf{XQueryColors} functions take pixel values in the \textit{pixel} member of \textbf{XColor} structures and store in the structures the RGB values for those pixels from the specified colormap. The values returned for an unallocated entry are undefined. These functions also set the \textit{flags} member in the \textbf{XColor} structure to all three colors. If a pixel is not a valid index into the specified colormap, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If more than one pixel is in error, the one that gets reported is arbitrary.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To query the RGB value of a single colormap cell, use \textbf{XQueryColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \begin{cppcode}
                int XQueryColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XColor *def_in_out
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{def\_in\_out}: Specifies and returns the RGB values for the pixel specified in the structure.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XQueryColor} function returns the current RGB value for the pixel in the \textbf{XColor} structure and sets the \textbf{DoRed}, \textbf{DoGreen}, and \textbf{DoBlue} flags.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XQueryColor} can generate \textbf{BadColor} and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To query the RGB values of multiple colormap cells, use \textbf{XQueryColors}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                int XQueryColors(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XColor defs_in_out[],
                    int ncolors
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{defs\_in\_out}: Specifies and returns an array of color definition structures for the pixels specified in the structures.
                \item \textit{ncolors}: Specifies the number of \textbf{XColor} structures in the color definition array.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XQueryColors} function returns the RGB value for each pixel in each \textbf{XColor} structure and sets the \textbf{DoRed}, \textbf{DoGreen}, and \textbf{DoBlue} flags in each structure.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XQueryColors} can generate \textbf{BadColor} and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To query the color of a single colormap cell in an arbitrary format, use \textbf{XcmsQueryColor}.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XcmsQueryColor(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XcmsColor *color_in_out,
                    XcmsColorFormat result_format
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{color\_in\_out}: Specifies the \textit{pixel} member that indicates the color cell to query. The color specification stored for the color cell is returned in this \textbf{XcmsColor} structure.
                \item \textit{result\_format}: Specifies the color format for the returned color specification.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XcmsQueryColor} function obtains the RGB value for the pixel value in the \textit{pixel} member of the specified \textbf{XcmsColor} structure and then converts the value to the target format as specified by the \textit{result\_format} argument. If the pixel is not a valid index in the specified colormap, a \textbf{BadValue} error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XcmsQueryColor} can generate \textbf{BadColor} and \textbf{BadValue} errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            To query the color of multiple colormap cells in an arbitrary format, use \textbf{XcmsQueryColors}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                Status XcmsQueryColors(
                    Display *display,
                    Colormap colormap,
                    XcmsColor colors_in_out[],
                    unsigned int ncolors,
                    XcmsColorFormat result_format
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item \textit{display}: Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item \textit{colormap}: Specifies the colormap.
                \item \textit{colors\_in\_out}: Specifies an array of \textbf{XcmsColor} structures, each \textit{pixel} member indicating the color cell to query. The color specifications for the color cells are returned in these structures.
                \item \textit{ncolors}: Specifies the number of \textbf{XcmsColor} structures in the color-specification array.
                \item \textit{result\_format}: Specifies the color format for the returned color specification.
            \end{itemize}
            \noindent
            The \textbf{XcmsQueryColors} function obtains the RGB values for pixel values in the \textit{pixel} members of \textbf{XcmsColor} structures and then converts the values to the target format as specified by the \textit{result\_format} argument.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            If a pixel is not a valid index into the specified colormap, a \textbf{BadValue} error results. If more than one pixel is in error, the one that gets reported is arbitrary.
            \bigbreak \noindent
            \textbf{XcmsQueryColors} can generate \textbf{BadColor} and \textbf{BadValue} errors.

    \end{itemize}


    \pagebreak 
    \unsect{7. Graphics context functions}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Intro}: A number of resources are used when performing graphics operations in X. Most information about performing graphics (for example, foreground color, background color, line style, and so on) is stored in resources called graphics contexts (GCs). Most graphics operations (see chapter 8) take a GC as an argument. Although in theory the X protocol permits sharing of GCs between applications, it is expected that applications will use their own GCs when performing operations. Sharing of GCs is highly discouraged because the library may cache GC state
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            Graphics operations can be performed to either windows or pixmaps, which collectively are called drawables. Each drawable exists on a single screen. A GC is created for a specific screen and drawable depth and can only be used with drawables of matching screen and depth.
        \item \textbf{Write-back cache}: A write-back cache is a caching technique where the system writes incoming data directly to the fast cache and instantly confirms the write is complete, deferring the update to the slower primary storage (like a hard drive or database) until a later time
        \item \textbf{Manipulating Graphics Context/State}: Most attributes of graphics operations are stored in GCs. These include line width, line style, plane mask, foreground, background, tile, stipple, clipping region, end style, join style, and so on. Graphics operations (for example, drawing lines) use these values to determine the actual drawing operation. 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            Xlib implements a write-back cache for all elements of a GC that are not resource IDs to allow Xlib to implement the transparent coalescing of changes to GCs. For example, a call to \textbf{XSetForeground} of a GC followed by a call to \textbf{XSetLineAttributes} results in only a single-change GC protocol request to the server. GCs are neither expected nor encouraged to be shared between client applications, so this write-back caching should present no problems. Applications cannot share GCs without external synchronization. Therefore, sharing GCs between applications is highly discouraged.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To set an attribute of a GC, set the appropriate member of the \textbf{XGCValues} structure and OR in the corresponding value bitmask in your subsequent calls to \textbf{XCreateGC.} The symbols for the value mask bits and the \textbf{XGCValues} structure are:
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                /* GC attribute value mask bits */
                #define GCFunction (1L<<0)
                #define GCPlaneMask (1L<<1)
                #define GCForeground (1L<<2)
                #define GCBackground (1L<<3)
                #define GCLineWidth (1L<<4)
                #define GCLineStyle (1L<<5)
                #define GCCapStyle (1L<<6)
                #define GCJoinStyle (1L<<7)
                #define GCFillStyle (1L<<8)
                #define GCFillRule (1L<<9)
                #define GCTile (1L<<10)
                #define GCStipple (1L<<11)
                #define GCTileStipXOrigin (1L<<12)
                #define GCTileStipYOrigin (1L<<13)
                #define GCFont (1L<<14)
                #define GCSubwindowMode (1L<<15)
                #define GCGraphicsExposures (1L<<16)
                #define GCClipXOrigin (1L<<17)
                #define GCClipYOrigin (1L<<18)
                #define GCClipMask (1L<<19)
                #define GCDashOffset (1L<<20)
                #define GCDashList (1L<<21)
                #define GCArcMode (1L<<22)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            /* Values */
            typedef struct {
                int function;                   /* logical operation */
                unsigned long plane_mask;       /* plane mask */
                unsigned long foreground;       /* foreground pixel */
                unsigned long background;       /* background pixel */
                int line_width;                 /* line width (in pixels) */
                int line_style;                 /* LineSolid, LineOnOffDash, LineDoubleDash */
                int cap_style;                  /* CapNotLast, CapButt, CapRound, CapProjecting */
                int join_style;                 /* JoinMiter, JoinRound, JoinBevel */
                int fill_style;                 /* FillSolid, FillTiled, FillStippled FillOpaqueStippled*/
                int fill_rule;                  /* EvenOddRule, WindingRule */
                int arc_mode;                   /* ArcChord, ArcPieSlice */
                Pixmap tile;                    /* tile pixmap for tiling operations */
                Pixmap stipple;                 /* stipple 1 plane pixmap for stippling */
                int ts_x_origin;                /* offset for tile or stipple operations */
                int ts_y_origin;
                Font font;                      /* default text font for text operations */
                int subwindow_mode;             /* ClipByChildren, IncludeInferiors */
                Bool graphics_exposures;        /* boolean, should exposures be generated */
                int clip_x_origin;              /* origin for clipping */
                int clip_y_origin;
                Pixmap clip_mask;               /* bitmap clipping; other calls for rects */
                int dash_offset;                /* patterned/dashed line information */
                char dashes;
            } XGCValues;
            \end{cppcode}



    \end{itemize}

    \pagebreak 
    \unsect{8. Graphics functions}

    \pagebreak 
    \unsect{9. Window and session manager functions}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Changing the parent of a window}: To change a window’s parent to another window on the same screen, use XReparentWindow. There is no way to move a window between screens.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XReparentWindow(Display* display, Window w, Window parent, int x, int y)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item $w$ Specifies the window.
                \item parent Specifies the parent window.
                \item $x$, $y$ Specify the $x$ and $y$ coordinates of the position in the new parent window.
            \end{itemize}
            If the specified window is mapped, XReparentWindow automatically performs an UnmapWindow request on it, removes it from its current position in the hierarchy, and inserts it as the child of the specified parent. The window is placed in the stacking order on top with respect to sibling windows.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            After reparenting the specified window, XReparentWindow causes the X server to generate a ReparentNotify event. The override\_redirect member returned in this event is set to the window’s corresponding attribute. Window manager clients usually should ignore this window if this member is set to True. Finally, if the specified window was originally mapped, the X server automatically performs a MapWindow request on it.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The X server performs normal exposure processing on formerly obscured windows. The X server might not generate Expose events for regions from the initial UnmapWindow request that are immediately obscured by the final MapWindow request. A BadMatch error results if:
            \begin{itemize}
                \item The new parent window is not on the same screen as the old parent window.
                \item The new parent window is the specified window or an inferior of the specified window.
                \item The new parent is InputOnly, and the window is not.
                \item The specified window has a ParentRelative background, and the new parent window is not the same depth as the specified window.
            \end{itemize}
            XReparentWindow can generate BadMatch and BadWindow errors.
        \item \textbf{Save set}: The save-set of a client is a list of other clients’ windows that, if they are inferiors of one of the client’s windows at connection close, should not be destroyed and should be remapped if they are unmapped. 
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To allow an application’s window to survive when a window manager that has reparented a window fails, Xlib provides the save-set functions that you can use to control the longevity of subwindows that are normally destroyed when the parent is destroyed. For example, a window manager that wants to add decoration to a window by adding a frame might reparent an application’s window. When the frame is destroyed, the application’s window should not be destroyed but be returned to its previous place in the window hierarchy
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The X server automatically removes windows from the save-set when they are destroyed.
        \item \textbf{Controlling the Lifetime of a Window}: To add or remove a window from the client’s save-set, use XChangeSaveSet
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XChangeSaveSet(Display* display, Window w, int change_mode)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item $w$ Specifies the window that you want to add to or delete from the client’s save-set.
                \item change\_mode Specifies the mode. You can pass SetModeInsert or SetModeDelete.
            \end{itemize}
            Depending on the specified mode, XChangeSaveSet either inserts or deletes the specified window from the client’s save-set. The specified window must have been created by some other client, or a BadMatch error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XChangeSaveSet can generate BadMatch, BadValue, and BadWindow errors
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To add a window to the client’s save-set, use XAddToSaveSet
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XAddToSaveSet(Display* display, Window w)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item $w$ Specifies the window that you want to add to the client’s save-set.
            \end{itemize}
            The XAddToSaveSet function adds the specified window to the client’s save-set. The specified window must have been created by some other client, or a BadMatch error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XAddToSaveSet can generate BadMatch and BadWindow errors.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To remove a window from the client’s save-set, use XRemoveFromSaveSet
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XRemoveFromSaveSet(Display* display, Window w)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item $w$ Specifies the window that you want to delete from the client’s save-set.
            \end{itemize}
            The XRemoveFromSaveSet function removes the specified window from the client’s save-set. The specified window must have been created by some other client, or a BadMatch error results.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XRemoveFromSaveSet can generate BadMatch and BadWindow errors.
        \item \textbf{Managing Installed Colormaps}: The X server maintains a list of installed colormaps. Windows using these colormaps are guaranteed to display with correct colors; windows using other colormaps may or may not display with correct colors. Xlib provides functions that you can use to install a colormap, uninstall a colormap, and obtain a list of installed colormaps.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            At any time, there is a subset of the installed maps that is viewed as an ordered list and is called the required list. The length of the required list is at most M, where M is the minimum number of installed colormaps specified for the screen in the connection setup. The required list is maintained as follows. When a colormap is specified to XInstallColormap, it is added to the head of the list; the list is truncated at the tail, if necessary, to keep its length to at most M. When a colormap is specified to XUninstallColormap and it is in the required list, it is removed from the list. A colormap is not added to the required list when it is implicitly installed by the X server, and the X server cannot implicitly uninstall a colormap that is in the required list.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To install a colormap, use XInstallColormap
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XInstallColormap(Display* display, Colormap colormap)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item colormap Specifies the colormap.
            \end{itemize}
            The XInstallColormap function installs the specified colormap for its associated screen. All windows associated with this colormap immediately display with true colors. You associated the windows with this colormap when you created them by calling XCreateWindow, XCreateSimpleWindow, XChangeWindowAttributes, or XSetWindowColormap.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the specified colormap is not already an installed colormap, the X server generates a ColormapNotify event on each window that has that colormap. In addition, for every other colormap that is installed as a result of a call to XInstallColormap, the X server generates a ColormapNotify event on each window that has that colormap.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XInstallColormap can generate a BadColor error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To uninstall a colormap, use XUninstallColormap.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XUninstallColormap(Display* display, Colormap colormap)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item colormap Specifies the colormap.
            \end{itemize}
            The XUninstallColormap function removes the specified colormap from the required list for its screen. As a result, the specified colormap might be uninstalled, and the X server might implicitly install or uninstall additional colormaps. Which colormaps get installed or uninstalled is server dependent except that the required list must remain installed.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the specified colormap becomes uninstalled, the X server generates a ColormapNotify event on each window that has that colormap. In addition, for every other colormap that is installed or uninstalled as a result of a call to XUninstallColormap, the X server generates a ColormapNotify event on each window that has that colormap.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XUninstallColormap can generate a BadColor error
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To obtain a list of the currently installed colormaps for a given screen, use XListInstalledColormaps
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            Colormap *XListInstalledColormaps(Display* display, Window w, int* num_return)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item $w$ Specifies the window that determines the screen.
                \item num\_return Returns the number of currently installed colormaps.
            \end{itemize}
            The XListInstalledColormaps function returns a list of the currently installed colormaps for the screen of the specified window. The order of the colormaps in the list is not significant and is no explicit indication of the required list. When the allocated list is no longer needed, free it by using XFree.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XListInstalledColormaps can generate a BadWindow error.
        \item \textbf{Setting and Retrieving the Font Search Path}: The set of fonts available from a server depends on a font search path. Xlib provides functions to set and retrieve the search path for a server.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To set the font search path, use XSetFontPath
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XSetFontPath(Display* display, char** directories, int ndirs)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item directories Specifies the directory path used to look for a font. Setting the path to the empty list restores the default path defined for the X server.
                \item ndirs Specifies the number of directories in the path.
            \end{itemize}
            The XSetFontPath function defines the directory search path for font lookup. There is only one search path per X server, not one per client. The encoding and interpretation of the strings are implementation-dependent, but typically they specify directories or font servers to be searched in the order listed. An X server is permitted to cache font information internally; for example, it might cache an entire font from a file and not check on subsequent opens of that font to see if the underlying font file has changed. However, when the font path is changed, the X server is guaranteed to flush all cached information about fonts for which there currently are no explicit resource IDs allocated. The meaning of an error from this request is implementation-dependent.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XSetFontPath can generate a BadValue error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To get the current font search path, use XGetFontPath
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            char** XGetFontPath(Display* display, int* npaths_return)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item npaths\_return Returns the number of strings in the font path array.
            \end{itemize}
            To free data returned by XGetFontPath, use XFreeFontPath
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XFreeFontPath(char** list)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item list Specifies the array of strings you want to free.
            \end{itemize}
            The XFreeFontPath function frees the data allocated by XGetFontPath
        \item \textbf{Grabbing the Server}: Xlib provides functions that you can use to grab and ungrab the server. These functions can be used to control processing of output on other connections by the window system server. While the server is grabbed, no processing of requests or close downs on any other connection will occur. A client closing its connection automatically ungrabs the server. Although grabbing the server is highly discouraged, it is sometimes necessary.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To grab the server, use \textbf{XGrabServer}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XGrabServer(Display* display)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \end{itemize}
            The XGrabServer function disables processing of requests and close downs on all other connections than the one this request arrived on. You should not grab the X server any more than is absolutely necessary.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To ungrab the server, use XUngrabServer
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XUngrabServer(Display* display)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
            \end{itemize}
            The XUngrabServer function restarts processing of requests and close downs on other connections. You should avoid grabbing the X server as much as possible.
        \item \textbf{Killing Clients}: Xlib provides a function to cause the connection to a client to be closed and its resources to be destroyed. To destroy a client, use XKillClient.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XKillClient(Display* display, XID resource)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item resource Specifies any resource associated with the client that you want to destroy or AllTemporary
            \end{itemize}
            The XKillClient function forces a close down of the client that created the resource if a valid resource is specified. If the client has already terminated in either RetainPermanent or RetainTemporary mode, all of the client’s resources are destroyed. If AllTemporary is specified, the resources of all clients that have terminated in RetainTemporary are destroyed. This permits implementation of window manager facilities that aid debugging. A client can set its close-down mode to RetainTemporary. If the client then crashes, its windows would not be destroyed. The programmer can then inspect the application’s window tree and use the window manager to destroy the zombie windows
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XKillClient can generate a BadValue error.
        \item \textbf{Controlling the Screen Saver}: Xlib provides functions that you can use to set or reset the mode of the screen saver, to force or activate the screen saver, or to obtain the current screen saver values.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To set the screen saver mode, use \textbf{XSetScreenSaver}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XSetScreenSaver(Display* display, int timeout, int interval, int prefer_blanking, int allow_exposures)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item timeout Specifies the timeout, in seconds, until the screen saver turns on.
                \item interval Specifies the interval, in seconds, between screen saver alterations.
                \item prefer\_blanking Specifies how to enable screen blanking. You can pass DontPreferBlanking, PreferBlanking, or DefaultBlanking.
                \item allow\_exposuresSpecifies the screen save control values. You can pass DontAllowExposures, AllowExposures, or DefaultExposures
            \end{itemize}
            Timeout and interval are specified in seconds. A timeout of 0 disables the screen saver (but an activated screen saver is not deactivated), and a timeout of −1 restores the default. Other negative values generate a BadValue error. If the timeout value is nonzero, XSetScreenSaver enables the screen saver. An interval of 0 disables the random-pattern motion. If no input from devices (keyboard, mouse, and so on) is generated for the specified number of timeout seconds once the screen saver is enabled, the screen saver is activated.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            For each screen, if blanking is preferred and the hardware supports video blanking, the screen simply goes blank. Otherwise, if either exposures are allowed or the screen can be regenerated without sending Expose events to clients, the screen is tiled with the root window background tile randomly re-origined each interval seconds. Otherwise, the screens’ state do not change, and the screen saver is not activated. The screen saver is deactivated, and all screen states are restored at the next keyboard or pointer input or at the next call to XForceScreenSaver with mode ScreenSaverReset
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            If the server-dependent screen saver method supports periodic change, the interval argument serves as a hint about how long the change period should be, and zero hints that no periodic change should be made. Examples of ways to change the screen include scrambling the colormap periodically, moving an icon image around the screen periodically, or tiling the screen with the root window background tile, randomly re-origined periodically.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XSetScreenSaver can generate a BadValue error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To force the screen saver on or off, use \textbf{XForceScreenSaver}.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
            XForceScreenSaver(Display* display, int mode)
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item mode Specifies the mode that is to be applied. You can pass ScreenSaverActive or ScreenSaverReset
            \end{itemize}
            If the specified mode is ScreenSaverActive and the screen saver currently is deactivated, XForceScreenSaver activates the screen saver even if the screen saver had been disabled with a timeout of zero. If the specified mode is ScreenSaverReset and the screen saver currently is enabled, XForceScreenSaver deactivates the screen saver if it was activated, and the activation timer is reset to its initial state (as if device input had been received).
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            XForceScreenSaver can generate a BadValue error.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To activate the screen saver, use XActivateScreenSaver.
            \begin{cppcode}
                XActivateScreenSaver(Display* display)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To reset the screen saver, use XResetScreenSaver.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XResetScreenSaver(Display* display)
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            To get the current screen saver values, use XGetScreenSaver
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                XGetScreenSaver(
                    Display* display,
                    int* timeout_return,
                    int* interval_return,
                    int* prefer_blanking_return,
                    int* allow_exposures_return
                )
            \end{cppcode}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item display Specifies the connection to the X server.
                \item timeout\_return Returns the timeout, in seconds, until the screen saver turns on.
                \item interval\_return Returns the interval between screen saver invocations.
                \item prefer\_blanking\_return Returns the current screen blanking preference (DontPreferBlanking, PreferBlanking, or DefaultBlanking).
                \item allow\_exposures\_return Returns the current screen save control value (DontAllowExposures, AllowExposures, or DefaultExposures).
            \end{itemize}



    \end{itemize}

    \pagebreak 
    \unsect{10. Events}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Events}: In X11, events are messages from the X server to clients.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            Your program is an X client. The X server owns the display, windows, keyboard, mouse, screen resources, and window tree. When something happens, the server may place an event into your client’s event queue.
            \begin{itemize}
                \item A key was pressed.
                \item The pointer moved.
                \item A window was created, mapped, unmapped, destroyed, resized, or moved.
                \item A window needs repainting.
                \item A client changed a property.
                \item A client asked the window manager for something.
                \item The input focus changed.
                \item The pointer entered or left a window
            \end{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Events are not automatically delivered to everyone}: The X server does not send every event to every client. That would be wasteful and ambiguous. Instead, each client declares interest in certain event categories on certain windows. This is done through event masks. An event mask says “For this window, send me these kinds of events.”
        \item \textbf{Event types}: An event is data generated asynchronously by the X server as a result of some device activity or as side effects of a request sent by an Xlib function. Device-related events propagate from the source window to ancestor windows until some client application has selected that event type or until the event is explicitly discarded. The X server generally sends an event to a client application only if the client has specifically asked to be informed of that event type, typically by setting the event-mask attribute of the window. The mask can also be set when you create a window or by changing the window’s event-mask. You can also mask out events that would propagate to ancestor windows by manipulating the do-not-propagate mask of the window’s attributes. However, \textbf{MappingNotify} events are always sent to all clients.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            n event type describes a specific event generated by the X server. For each event type, a corresponding constant name is defined in <X11/X.h>, which is used when referring to an event type. The following table lists the event category and its associated event type or types. 
            \begin{center}
                \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}XX@{}}
                    \toprule
                    \textbf{Event Category}& \textbf{Event Type} \\
                    \midrule
                    Keyboard events &KeyPress, KeyRelease\\[2ex]
                    Pointer events &ButtonPress, ButtonRelease, MotionNotify\\[2ex]
                    Window crossing events &EnterNotify, LeaveNotify\\[2ex]
                    Input focus events &FocusIn, FocusOut\\[2ex]
                    Keymap state notification event &KeymapNotify\\[2ex]
                    Exposure events &Expose, GraphicsExpose, NoExpose\\[2ex]
                    Structure control events &CirculateRequest, ConfigureRequest, MapRequest, ResizeRequest \\[2ex]
                    Window state notification events &CirculateNotify, ConfigureNotify, CreateNotify, DestroyNotify, GravityNotify, MapNotify, MappingNotify, ReparentNotify, UnmapNotify, VisibilityNotify\\[2ex]
                    Colormap state notification event& ColormapNotify\\[2ex]
                    Client communication events &ClientMessage, PropertyNotify, SelectionClear, SelectionNotify, SelectionRequest  \\
                    \bottomrule
                \end{tabularx}
            \end{center}
        \item \textbf{Event structures}: For each event type, a corresponding structure is declared in <X11/Xlib.h>. All the event structures have the following common members:
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                typedef struct {
                    int type;
                    unsigned long serial;   /* # of last request processed by server */
                    Bool send_event;        /* true if this came from a SendEvent request */
                    Display *display;       /* Display the event was read from */
                    Window window;
                } XAnyEvent;
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The type member is set to the event type constant name that uniquely identifies it. For example, when the X server reports a GraphicsExpose event to a client application, it sends an XGraphicsExposeEvent structure with the type member set to GraphicsExpose. The display member is set to a pointer to the display the event was read on. The send\_event member is set to True if the event came from a SendEvent protocol request. The serial member is set from the serial number reported in the protocol but expanded from the 16-bit least-significant bits to a full 32-bit value. The window member is set to the window that is most useful to toolkit dispatchers.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The X server can send events at any time in the input stream. Xlib stores any events received while waiting for a reply in an event queue for later use. Xlib also provides functions that allow you to check events in the event queue
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            In addition to the individual structures declared for each event type, the XEvent structure is a union of the individual structures declared for each event type. Depending on the type, you should access members of each event by using the XEvent union.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            \begin{cppcode}
                typedef union _XEvent {
                    int type;           /* must not be changed */
                    XAnyEvent xany;
                    XKeyEvent xkey;
                    XButtonEvent xbutton;
                    XMotionEvent xmotion;
                    XCrossingEvent xcrossing;
                    XFocusChangeEvent xfocus;
                    XExposeEvent xexpose;
                    XGraphicsExposeEvent xgraphicsexpose;
                    XNoExposeEvent xnoexpose;
                    XVisibilityEvent xvisibility;
                    XCreateWindowEvent xcreatewindow;
                    XDestroyWindowEvent xdestroywindow;
                    XUnmapEvent xunmap;
                    XMapEvent xmap;
                    XMapRequestEvent xmaprequest;
                    XReparentEvent xreparent;
                    XConfigureEvent xconfigure;
                    XGravityEvent xgravity;
                    XResizeRequestEvent xresizerequest;
                    XConfigureRequestEvent xconfigurerequest;
                    XCirculateEvent xcirculate;
                    XCirculateRequestEvent xcirculaterequest;
                    XPropertyEvent xproperty;
                    XSelectionClearEvent xselectionclear;
                    XSelectionRequestEvent xselectionrequest;
                    XSelectionEvent xselection;
                    XColormapEvent xcolormap;
                    XClientMessageEvent xclient;
                    XMappingEvent xmapping;
                    XErrorEvent xerror;
                    XKeymapEvent xkeymap;
                    long pad[24];
                } XEvent;
            \end{cppcode}
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            An XEvent structure’s first entry always is the type member, which is set to the event type. The second member always is the serial number of the protocol request that generated the event. The third member always is send\_event, which is a Bool that indicates if the event was sent by a different client. The fourth member always is a display, which is the display that the event was read from. Except for keymap events, the fifth member always is a window, which has been carefully selected to be useful to toolkit dispatchers. To avoid breaking toolkits, the order of these first five entries is not to change. Most events also contain a time member, which is the time at which an event occurred. In addition, a pointer to the generic event must be cast before it is used to access any other information in the structure.
        \item \textbf{Event Masks}: Clients select event reporting of most events relative to a window. To do this, pass an event mask to an Xlib event-handling function that takes an event\_mask argument. The bits of the event mask are defined in <X11/X.h>. Each bit in the event mask maps to an event mask name, which describes the event or events you want the X server to return to a client application.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            Unless the client has specifically asked for them, most events are not reported to clients when they are generated. Unless the client suppresses them by setting graphics-exposures in the GC to False, GraphicsExpose and NoExpose are reported by default as a result of XCopyPlane and XCopyArea. SelectionClear, SelectionRequest, SelectionNotify, or ClientMessage cannot be masked. Selection-related events are only sent to clients cooperating with selections. When the keyboard or pointer mapping is changed, MappingNotify is always sent to clients.
            \begin{center}
                \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}lX@{}}
                    \toprule
                    \textbf{Event Mask}& \textbf{Circumstances} \\
                    \midrule
                    NoEventMask& No events wanted\\[2ex]
                    KeyPressMask& Keyboard down events wanted\\[2ex]
                    KeyReleaseMask& Keyboard up events wanted\\[2ex]
                    ButtonPressMask& Pointer button down events wanted\\[2ex]
                    ButtonReleaseMask& Pointer button up events wanted\\[2ex]
                    EnterWindowMask& Pointer window entry events wanted\\[2ex]
                    LeaveWindowMask& Pointer window leave events wanted\\[2ex]
                    PointerMotionMask& Pointer motion events wanted\\[2ex]
                    PointerMotionHintMask& Pointer motion hints wanted\\[2ex]
                    Button1MotionMask& Pointer motion while button 1 down\\[2ex]
                    Button2MotionMask& Pointer motion while button 2 down\\[2ex]
                    Button3MotionMask& Pointer motion while button 3 down\\[2ex]
                    Button4MotionMask& Pointer motion while button 4 down\\[2ex]
                    Button5MotionMask& Pointer motion while button 5 down\\[2ex]
                    ButtonMotionMask& Pointer motion while any button down\\[2ex]
                    KeymapStateMask& Keyboard state wanted at window entry and focus in\\[2ex]
                    ExposureMask& Any exposure wanted\\[2ex]
                    VisibilityChangeMask& Any change in visibility wanted\\[2ex]
                    StructureNotifyMask& Any change in window structure wanted\\[2ex]
                    ResizeRedirectMask& Redirect resize of this window\\[2ex]
                    SubstructureNotifyMask& Substructure notification wanted\\[2ex]
                    SubstructureRedirectMask& Redirect structure requests on children\\[2ex]
                    FocusChangeMask& Any change in input focus wanted\\[2ex]
                    PropertyChangeMask& Any change in property wanted\\[2ex]
                    ColormapChangeMask& Any change in colormap wanted\\[2ex]
                    OwnerGrabButtonMask& Automatic grabs should activate with owner\_events set to True \\
                    \bottomrule
                \end{tabularx}
            \end{center}
        \item \textbf{Event processing overview}: The event reported to a client application during event processing depends on which event masks you provide as the event-mask attribute for a window. For some event masks, there is a one-to-one correspondence between the event mask constant and the event type constant. For example, if you pass the event mask ButtonPressMask, the X server sends back only ButtonPress events. Most events contain a time member, which is the time at which an event occurred.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            In other cases, one event mask constant can map to several event type constants. For example, if you pass the event mask SubstructureNotifyMask, the X server can send back CirculateNotify, ConfigureNotify, CreateNotify, DestroyNotify, GravityNotify, MapNotify, ReparentNotify, or UnmapNotify events.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            In another case, two event masks can map to one event type. For example, if you pass either PointerMotionMask or ButtonMotionMask, the X server sends back a MotionNotify event.
            \bigbreak \noindent 
            The following table lists the event mask, its associated event type or types, and the structure name associated with the event type. Some of these structures actually are typedefs to a generic structure that is shared between two event types. Note that N.A. appears in columns for which the information is not applicable
            \begin{center}
                \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}XlXl@{}}
                    \toprule
                    \textbf{Event Mask}& \textbf{Event Type}& \textbf{Structure} &\textbf{Generic Structure} \\
                    \midrule
                    ButtonMotionMask &MotionNotify &XPointerMovedEvent &XMotionEvent \\[2ex]
                    Button1MotionMask & & & \\[2ex]
                    Button2MotionMask & & &\\[2ex]
                    Button3MotionMask & & &\\[2ex]
                    Button4MotionMask & & &\\[2ex]
                    Button5MotionMask & & &\\[2ex]
                    ButtonPressMask &ButtonPress &XButtonPressedEvent &XButtonEvent\\[2ex]
                    ButtonReleaseMask &ButtonRelease &XButtonReleasedEvent &XButtonEvent\\[2ex]
                    ColormapChangeMask &ColormapNotify &XColormapEvent &\\[2ex]
                    EnterWindowMask &EnterNotify &XEnterWindowEvent &XCrossingEvent\\[2ex]
                    LeaveWindowMask &LeaveNotify &XLeaveWindowEvent &XCrossingEvent\\[2ex]
                    ExposureMask &Expose &XExposeEvent & \\[2ex]
                    GCGraphicsExposures in GC & GraphicsExpose & XGraphicsExposeEvent & \\[2ex]
                                              & NoExpose &XNoExposeEvent & \\
                    \bottomrule
                \end{tabularx}
            \end{center}

            \begin{center}
                \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}XlXl@{}}
                    \toprule
                    \textbf{Event Mask}& \textbf{Event Type}& \textbf{Structure} &\textbf{Generic Structure} \\
                    \midrule
                    FocusChangeMask &FocusIn &XFocusInEvent &XFocusChangeEvent\\[2ex]
                                    &FocusOut &XFocusOutEvent &XFocusChangeEvent  \\
                    KeymapStateMask &KeymapNotify &XKeymapEvent & \\[2ex]
                    KeyPressMask &KeyPress &XKeyPressedEvent &XKeyEvent\\[2ex]
                    KeyReleaseMask &KeyRelease &XKeyReleasedEvent &XKeyEvent\\[2ex]
                    OwnerGrabButtonMask & N.A. & N.A. & \\[2ex]
                    PointerMotionMask &MotionNotify &XPointerMovedEvent &XMotionEvent\\[2ex]
                    PointerMotionHintMask &N.A. &  N.A. & \\[2ex]
                    PropertyChangeMask &PropertyNotify &XPropertyEvent & \\[2ex]
                    ResizeRedirectMask &ResizeRequest & XResizeRequestEvent &\\[2ex]
